قال وما اجرى مجرى الخطاء مثل النائم ينقلب على رجل فيقتله فحكمه حكم الخطاء في الشرع واما القتل بسبب كحافر البير وواضع الحجر فى غير ملكه وموجبه اذا تلف فيه ادمى الدية على العاقلة لانه سبب وهو متعد فيه فانزل موقعا فوجبت الدية ولا كفارة فيه ولا يتعلق به حرمان الميراث التلف ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو قتل خطا کے قائم مقام ہے وہ جیسے سونے والا کسی شخص پر پلٹ جائے پس اس کو مار ڈالے تو اس کا حکم قتل خطاء کا حکم ہے شریعت میں اور بہر حال قتل سبب کے ذریعہ جیسے اپنی ملک کے غیر میں کنواں کھودنے والا اور پتھر رکھنے والا اور اس کا موجب جب کہ کوئی آدمی اس میں مرجائے عاقلہ پر دیت ہے اس لیے کہ یہ تکلف کا سبب ہے اور قاتل اس میں متعدی ہے تو اس کو گرانے والے اور دھکیلنے والے کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا پس دیت واجب ہو گی اور اس میں کفارہ نہیں ہے اور اس کے ساتھ میراث سے محروم ہو نا متعلق نہیں ہوتا ۔ تشریح قتل خطا سے فراغت کے بعد مصنف اس قتل کا بیان فرماتے ہیں جو تل خطا کے قائم مقام ہے۔ جیسے آدمی سور ہا تھا اس نے کروٹ لی مگر کسی آدمی کے اوپر پڑ گیا جس کی وجہ سے وہ مر گیا تو اس کا حکم وہی ہو گا جو قتل خطأ ہوتا ہے اس کے بعد پھر مصنف نے قتل کا سبب ذکر فرمایا۔ جیسے کسی آدمی نے ایسی زمین میں کنواں کھودا جو اس کی ملک نہیں ہے اور کوئی اس میں گر کر مر گیا یا اس نے ایسی ہی زمین میں پتھر رکھ دیا جس سے ٹکرا کر کوئی مر گیا تو اس میں عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ کھودنا اور پتھر رکھنا ہلاکت کا سبب ہے۔ اور جب سبب کا مرتکب متعدی ہوتا ہے تو سبب کو علت کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں اس کی تعدی ظاہر ہے لہذا یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ گویا اس نے خود اس کو کنویں میں ڈالا ہے اور خود اس کو پتھر پر دھکیل دیا ہے لہذاد بیت واجب ہوگی البتہ اس میں کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور نہ یہ قاتل میراث سے محروم ہو گا ۔ تنبیہ موقعاً : کنویں میں گرانے والا ، دافعا پتھر پر پھینکنے والا ۔
He said: And what runs in the course of khata, like a sleeping person rolling onto a man and killing him, then its ruling is the ruling of khata in the Shari'ah. As for killing by a cause, like a digger of a well or a placer of a stone in other than his property, and its consequence when a person perishes in it, diyah is on the aqilah because it is a cause and he is transgressive in it, so he is placed in the position of one who throws or pushes, thus diyah is obligatory, and there is no kaffarah in it, and deprivation of inheritance is not attached to it.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah (via Al-Quduri) defining two categories of homicide that are treated as accidental (khata) in their legal consequences. First, the sleeper: a person who rolls over in sleep onto another causing death is ruled as khata, meaning no qisas, only diyah on the aqilah. Second, causal homicide: digging a well or placing a stone on land you do not own, and someone dies as a result. Since the act is transgressive (because done on non-owned land), the causer is treated as if he directly threw or pushed the victim, making diyah obligatory on the aqilah. However, unlike direct khata, there is no kaffarah (expiation) and no deprivation of inheritance for the killer, because the killing is not actual but only by cause. The commentary explains that the transgression (ta'addi) makes the cause equivalent to a direct act for financial liability (daman) but not for spiritual or inheritance matters.

Key Terms
ما اجرى مجرى الخطاء (ma ajra majra al-khata): Acts that are treated legally as accidental homicide, though not strictly khata, due to similarity in absence of intent to kill.
القتل بسبب (al-qatl bi-sabab): Killing by a cause where the death results from an intermediate factor created by the agent, not a direct act.
العاقلة (al-aqilah): The male paternal relatives of the killer who are liable to pay diyah in cases of qatl khata and qatl sabab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Kaffarah is wajib on the aqilah.

Key Takeaway
Causal homicide with transgression triggers diyah on the aqilah but not kaffarah or inheritance deprivation, distinguishing it from direct accidental killing.

6 min
Causal Homicide Only Annexed for Liability, Not Kaffarah or Inheritance
Inter-madhhab debate on annexing causal homicide to khata

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes between financial liability and spiritual/familial rulings in causal homicide, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The annexation of causal homicide to accidental killing is only partial — limited to financial liability, not spiritual expiation or inheritance.

The Shafi'i school argues that if the Shari'ah treats the cause of death as a killer, all rulings of accidental killing should apply — diyah, kaffarah, and inheritance deprivation. The Hanafi school responds with a nuanced position: the annexation is limited to financial liability (daman) because the actual killing is absent. For kaffarah and inheritance, which depend on sin and direct agency, the original principle that no killing occurred remains.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that causal homicide should be fully annexed to khata because the Shari'ah places the causer in the rank of a killer (qatil). Therefore, all rulings of khata — diyah, kaffarah, and inheritance deprivation — must apply.
The Shafi'i view relies on the apparent meaning of the Shari'ah's treatment of the causer.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school objects that actual killing is non-existent from the causer. The cause is not the same as a direct act. The Shari'ah only annexes the cause to a direct act for financial liability due to transgression, not for spiritual or familial rulings.
The Hanafi proof is based on the reality that the causer did not directly kill; he is only a cause.
3
Trace the Hanafi line: separation of rulings
For dhaman (financial liability), the causer is treated as a killer by qiyas because of the transgressive act. For kaffarah and inheritance, the original principle (absence of killing) remains because these rulings depend on actual sin and direct agency. The causer is sinful for the transgressive act (e.g., digging) but not sinful for the death itself.
Kaffarah is expiation for the sin of killing; inheritance deprivation is also tied to sin. Since there is no sin of killing, neither applies.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a person who digs a well in non-owned land causing death must pay diyah (via aqilah) but does not need to observe kaffarah (fasting or freeing a slave) and inherits from the victim if he is an heir. Under the Shafi'i view, he would need kaffarah and would be barred from inheritance.
The practical difference clarifies the importance of the Hanafi distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و قال الشافعي يلحق بالخطأ فى احكامه لان الشرع انزله قاتلا ولنا ان القتل معدوم منه حقيقة فالحق به في حق الضمان فبقى في حق غيره على الاصل وهو ان كان ياثم بالحفر فى غير ملكه لا يأثم بالموت على ما قالوا وهذه كفارة ذنب القتل وكذا الحرمان بسبه ترجمہ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس کو (قتل سبب کو قتل خطا کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جائے گا اس کے احکام میں اس لئے کہ شریعت نے اس کو قاتل کے درجہ میں اتار دیا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کی طرف سے حقیقت قتل معدوم ہے تو اس کو ضمان کے حق میں قتل خطا کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا گیا ہے۔ پس منمان کے حق میں قتل سبب اصل پر برقرار رہے گا اور سبب مسبب اگر چہ غیر ملک میں کنواں کھودنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا ( لیکن ) موت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار نہ ہو گا جیسا کہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اور یہ کفارہ قتل ) قتل کے گناہ کا کفارہ ہے اور ایسے بی میراث سے حرمان گناہ کے سبب سے ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک قتل سبب میں صرف دیت ہے کنارہ نہیں اور نہ حرمان ارٹ ہے امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ بھی ہے اور میراث سے محروم ہونا بھی ہے کیونکہ شریعت نے جو اس کو قتل قرار دیا ہے اور قتل کا بلکا درجہ قتل خطا ہے بندا اقتل خطا کے احکام اس پر جاری ہوں گے۔ ہم نے جواب دیا کہ حقیقہ قاتل کی جانب سے قتل معدوم ہے البتہ یہ صرف قتل کا سبب ہے تو اس سبب ہونے کی وجہ سے ہم نے اس کے اوپر اور ہم پر بر رکھا او پر دویست واجب کردی لیکن کفارہ اور حرمان ارث کے بارے میں ہم نے اس کو اس کی حقیقت پر برقرار رکھا کہ یہ اس کی جانب سے قتل نہیں ہے بنا نہ کفار وہوگا اور نہ میراث سے محروم ہو گا۔ اور کفار قتل اور میراث سے حرمان جب ہوتا ہے کہ قتل کی وحدت گنہگار ہو اور یہ موت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ہی نہیں بلکہ غیر ملک میں کنواں کھود نے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہے۔
And al-Shafi'i said: It is annexed to khata in its rulings because the Shari'ah has placed him as a killer. And for us: the killing is non-existent from him in reality, so it was annexed to him in the right of dhaman, and it remains in other than that on the original principle, and he is sinful by digging in non-owned property, but he is not sinful by the death, as they said: and this is the kaffarah of the sin of killing, and likewise the deprivation of inheritance. Translation: And Shafi'i said that causal killing is annexed to accidental killing in its rulings because the Shari'ah has placed him in the rank of killer. Our evidence is that actual killing is non-existent from him, so it was annexed to khata only for the right of dhaman; for dhaman it remains on the original principle. The causer may be sinful for digging in non-owned land, but not sinful for the death, as the mashayikh said. Kaffarah is for the sin of killing and inheritance deprivation is also due to sin. In our view, causal homicide only has diyah, no kaffarah, no inheritance deprivation. Shafi'i says it has kaffarah and inheritance deprivation because the Shari'ah considers him a killer and the rank of khata applies, so all its rulings apply. We replied that actual killing is absent from the killer; it is only a cause. Due to being a cause we imposed diyah, but for kaffarah and inheritance we keep it on its original reality, so no kaffarah and no inheritance deprivation.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that causal homicide (like digging a well or placing a stone) should be fully annexed to khata (accidental killing) in all rulings—diyah, kaffarah, and inheritance deprivation—because the Shari'ah treats such a person as a killer (since he is the cause). The Hanafi position counters that killing is only real when the act directly causes death; here it is merely a cause. For financial liability (daman), the causer is indeed treated as a direct killer by analogy (the cause is placed in the position of a direct act due to transgression). However, for matters of sin and spiritual liability (kaffarah) and inheritance deprivation, which are tied to actual killing and sin, the original principle remains: since he did not actually kill, he is not sinful for the death (only for the transgressive act of digging), so kaffarah and inheritance deprivation do not apply. The commentary emphasizes that kaffarah is for the sin of killing, and inheritance deprivation is because of sin; here there is no sin of killing, only sin of transgression in digging. Thus the Hanafi position distinguishes between the financial aspect (daman) and the spiritual/familial aspects.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Financial liability, here specifically the obligation to pay diyah for causing death.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for certain sins, here the sin of killing; in qatl khata, kaffarah is freeing a slave or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling regarding kaffarah in causal homicide (qatl bi-sabab)?
A) Wajib
B) Not wajib because the causer is not sinful for the death
C) Not wajib because it is only for intentional killing
D) Not wajib because the aqilah pays it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, causal homicide triggers only financial liability (diyah), not spiritual expiation or inheritance deprivation, because the causer is not a direct killer.

Shibh Amd: Limited to Killing, Not Limbs
Legal maxim with talil (reasoning)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim on shibh amd to distinguish between intentional harm to life and intentional harm to limbs.

Core Idea
Shibh amd applies only to killing; all other bodily harm is treated as fully intentional.

This lesson introduces a crucial Hanafi maxim that limits the scope of shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing) to cases where life is taken. Understanding this maxim prevents the mistaken extension of lighter penalties to injuries, ensuring that intentional harm to limbs is always treated with the full severity of 'amd.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Maxim
Learn the Arabic text of the maxim: 'وما يكون شبه عمد في النفس فهو عمد فيما سواها'. This is the core rule.
The maxim contrasts two categories: 'nafs' (soul/life) and 'siwaha' (other than it, i.e., limbs).
2
Identify the Two Rulings
For the soul (killing), shibh amd is possible; for limbs and other parts, it is always 'amd (intentional).
3
Understand the 'Illa (Reason)
The reason given is that the destruction of the soul varies with the instrument used (some instruments are lethal, others are not), while the destruction of limbs is not instrument-specific—any implement can cause the same harm.
For example, an eye can be gouged out with a knife or a whip equally.
4
Apply to Examples
Test the maxim: A person strikes another on the leg with a light stick, intending only to cause pain but the leg breaks. The harm to the leg is 'amd, not shibh amd. If a person strikes another on the head with a stick and death occurs, it may be shibh amd if the stick is not ordinarily lethal.
The key is whether the specific result (death vs. injury) depends on the instrument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يكون شبه عمد في النفس فهو عمد فيما سواها لان اتلاف النفس يختلف باختلاف الآلة وما دونها لايختص اتلاقه بالة دون الة والله اعلم ترجمہ اور جو قتل نفس میں شبہ عمد ہو وہ نفس کے علاوہ میں قتل عمد ہے اس لئے کہ نفس کا اتلاف آلہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے مختلف وجہے ہوتا اور جونفس سے کم ہے اس کا اتلاف کسی ایک آلہ کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے نہ کہ دوسرے آلہ کے ساتھ ۔ والعداء تشریح کبھی تو قتل ہوتا ہے اور کبھی اعضاء کو توڑنا اور کا ناوغیرہ ہوتا ہے جس کا بیان آگے آرہا ہے۔ تو مصنفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قتل کا معد اور شبہ عد ہو نا صرف قتل نفس کے بارے میں ہے لیکن اعضاء کو توڑنے اور کانٹے میں سب حد ہی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ بات قتل کے اندر تو چلے گی کہ اس سے اس کا ارادہ قتل کا تھا یا نہیں قطع اعضاء میں نہیں چلے گی ، کیونکہ آنکھ جیسے چھری سے چھوڑ ہی جاتی ہے ایسے ہی کوڑے اور چھری سے چھوڑی جاتی ہے۔
And what is shibh amd regarding the soul, it is amd regarding other than it, because the destruction of the soul differs according to the instrument, and what is less than it (the soul) its destruction is not specific to one instrument rather than another. And Allah knows best. Translation: And the killing that is quasi-intentional in respect of the soul is intentional in respect of other than the soul, because the destruction of the soul varies with the difference of instrument, but the destruction of that which is less than the soul (i.e., limbs) is not restricted to a particular instrument. Commentary: Sometimes killing occurs, and sometimes breaking limbs and gouging eyes etc., which will be explained later. The author says that the category of shibh amd only applies to killing of the soul; for breaking limbs and cutting etc., it is all considered intentional, because the issue of intent for killing (whether he intended to kill or not) applies, but for cutting limbs it does not apply, because an eye can be cut out with a knife as well as with a whip, etc.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a legal maxim from the Hanafi school that defines the scope of shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing). It states that the classification of a homicide as shibh amd (where the act is intentional but the death is not clearly intended) only applies when the victim's soul (life) is taken. For injuries less than death—such as cutting off limbs, gouging eyes—the ruling is always 'amd (intentional) regardless of the instrument used. The reason ('illa) is that killing can vary depending on the instrument: a weapon is usually intended to kill, whereas a stick may not be. Thus a distinction is made. But for limbs, any instrument can cause the same harm, so the intent to harm is presumed, and it is always treated as intentional. The commentary illustrates that an eye can be lost by a knife or a whip; therefore the distinction of instrument does not change the ruling. This maxim prevents the extension of shibh amd (which carries lighter penalties) to bodily harm.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh amd): Quasi-intentional killing: the act is intentional but the weapon is not ordinarily lethal, so the intent to kill is not certain.
نفس (nafs): The soul or life of a human being; here specifically the taking of life.
سواها (siwaha): Other than the soul, i.e., limbs, organs, and parts of the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim, what is the ruling on a person who uses a whip to gouge someone's eye?
A) It is shibh amd because the whip is not a lethal instrument.
B) It is amd (intentional) because the destruction of limbs does not depend on the instrument.
C) It is khata if the person did not intend to hit the eye.
D) It is mubah because the whip is not a weapon.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim restricts shibh amd to killing; all other bodily harm is always classified as 'amd due to the instrument-independence of such injuries.

Killing a Muslim Mistaken for a Polytheist in Battle
Ruling on killing a Muslim by mistake in battle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for mistakenly killing a Muslim in battle and identify the evidence from Quran 4:92 that supports it.

Core Idea
Mistaken identity in battle is accidental killing: no qisas, but diyah and kaffarah are obligatory.

In the chaos of battle, it is possible for a Muslim soldier to inadvertently kill a fellow Muslim, mistaking him for an enemy. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling on this scenario, distinguishing it from intentional homicide. This lesson will examine the ruling as stated by Imam Muhammad in al-Hidayah and its proof from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Focus on the specific act: a Muslim kills another Muslim in battle, mistakenly thinking he is a polytheist. The ruling is that qisas (retaliatory execution) is not required, but diyah (blood money) and kaffarah (expiation) are wajib (obligatory).
This ruling applies only when the killer genuinely believed the victim was an enemy combatant.
2
Locate the Dalil
Identify the legal proof cited: Quran 4:92, which states that whoever kills a believer by mistake must free a slave and pay diyah to the family. The verse is directly quoted in the text.
The Quranic text is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) and qat'i al-dalalah (clear meaning) for the Hanafis.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the verse proves the ruling: The verse commands diyah and kaffarah for killing a believer, and does not prescribe qisas. Since the verse speaks of a believer, it covers cases where the victim was believed to be a non-believer but was actually a Muslim. The command for diyah and kaffarah indicates that qisas is not applicable.
Hanafi usul holds that if the Quran prescribes a specific penalty for an act, that penalty is exclusive unless otherwise indicated.
4
Confirm the Authority Level
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah (the transmitted core texts) of the Hanafi school, specifically from Imam Muhammad. It is the mufta bihi (operative) position, and there is no significant intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.
The ruling is also consistent with other schools (muttafaq alayh), though their detailed conditions may differ slightly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میدان جہاد میں مسلمانوں اور مشرکوں میں لڑائی کی زیادتی سے لوگ ایک دوسرے میں گھس گئے پھر ایک مسلمان کے ہاتھ سے ان جانے دوسرا مسلمان شہید ہو گیا تو قصاص نہیں ہوگا
قال واذا التقى الصفان من المسلمين والمشركين فقتل مسلم مسلما ظن انه مشرک فلا قود عليه وعليه الكفارة لان هذا احد نو عى الخطأ على ما بيناه والخطأ نوعيه لا يوجب القود ويوجب الكفارة وكذالدية على ما نطق به نص الكتاب
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جب مسلمانوں اور مشرکین کی دونوں صفوں کی مٹھ بھیڑ ہوگئی پس مسلمان کسی مسلمان کو مشرک سمجھ کر قتل کر دیا تو اس پر قصاص نہیں ہے اور اس پر کفارہ ہے اس لئے کہ یہ خطا کی دونوٹس میں سے ایک ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ اور خطاء اپنی دونوں کے ساتھ قصاص کو واجب نہیں کرتا اور کفارہ اور دیت کو واجب کرتا جیسا کہ نص کتاب ناطق ہے۔ تشریح مسلمانوں اور مشرکین کی صف بندی منتشر ہو کر لڑائی ہو گئی کسی مسلمان نے کسی کو مشرک سمجھ کر قتل کر دیا حالانکہ وہ مقتول مسلمان ہے تو قاتل پر قصاص نہیں صرف کفارہ اور دیت ہے کیونکہ یہ خطاء فی القصد ہے اور جو بھی قسم ہو قتل خطاء میں قصاص نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دیت اور کفارہ واجب ہوا کرتا ہے فرمانِ باری سے یہی ثابت ہے ارشاد ہے۔ ومن قتل مؤمنا فتحرير رقبة وديه مسلمة الى اهله
In the battlefield, due to the intensity of fighting between Muslims and polytheists, people got mixed, then a Muslim accidentally killed another Muslim thinking he was a polytheist, so there is no qisas. He said: When the two ranks of Muslims and polytheists meet, then a Muslim kills a Muslim thinking he is a polytheist, there is no qisas upon him, and upon him is kaffarah, because this is one of the two types of error (khata') as we have explained. And error in its two types does not necessitate qisas but necessitates kaffarah and likewise diyah, as the text of the Book (Quran) states. Translation: Muhammad said: And when the two ranks of Muslims and polytheists clash, then a Muslim kills a Muslim thinking he is a polytheist, then there is no qisas on him but kaffarah is due, because this is one of the two types of error according to the detail we have explained. And error in its two types does not necessitate qisas but necessitates kaffarah and diyah, as the text of the Book is explicit. Commentary: The ranks of Muslims and polytheists got mixed and fighting occurred. A Muslim killed someone thinking he was a polytheist whereas the victim was Muslim. So upon the killer, there is no qisas, only kaffarah and diyah, because this is khata' fi al-qasd (error in intention). And whichever type of qatl khata', qisas is not wajib but diyah and kaffarah are wajib. This is established from the divine command: 'And whoever kills a believer, then freeing a slave and diyah paid to his family' (Quran 4:92).
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Quran and Imam Muhammad's statement. The scenario is a battlefield where Muslims and polytheists are intermingled, and a Muslim kills another Muslim mistakenly believing him to be a polytheist. The ruling: no qisas, but diyah (blood money) and kaffarah (expiation) are wajib. The reason is that this falls under qatl khata' (accidental killing), specifically 'khata' fi al-qasd' (error in intention) – the killer intended to kill a polytheist but erroneously killed a Muslim. In Hanafi law, accidental killing (both types: khata' fi al-fi'l and khata' fi al-qasd) does not warrant qisas but requires diyah and kaffarah. The Quranic verse cited (4:92) supports this: freeing a slave and paying diyah to the family. This is a standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
خطاء فی القصد (khata' fi al-qasd): Error in intention: intending to kill one person but killing another.
نوعا الخطأ (naw'a al-khata'): Two types of error: error in act and error in intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a Muslim who kills another Muslim in battle mistakenly thinking he is a polytheist?
A) Qisas is wajib
B) Only diyah is wajib
C) Diyah and kaffarah are wajib, no qisas
D) No liability at all

Key Takeaway
Mistaken killing of a Muslim in battle is accidental (khata') and requires diyah and kaffarah, not qisas.

Multiple Causes of Death: One-Third Diyah on the Stranger
Ruling on apportionment of diyah when death results from multiple causes, including self-harm and animal attacks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school imposes only one-third diyah on a stranger when multiple causes (self-inflicted, animal attack, and human wound) contribute to death, and apply the principle of hadar (legal inconsequentiality) to distinguish between causes.

Core Idea
When self-harm and animal attacks combine with a human wound to cause death, the stranger pays only one-third of the diyah because his act is the only one with worldly legal consequence.

This lesson addresses a nuanced case in Hanafi criminal law: when a person dies from a combination of self-inflicted injury, a wound inflicted by another person, and attacks by a lion and a snake. The question is whether the human assailant must pay the full diyah (blood money) or only a portion. The Hanafi ruling, based on the reasoning of Imam Muhammad, is that the stranger pays one-third of the full diyah. This apportionment follows from the principle that certain acts—self-harm and animal attacks—are 'hadar' (legally inconsequential) in worldly matters, leaving only the stranger's act as a legally effective cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and their actions
List all participants: the victim himself (self-inflicted wound), the stranger (ajnabi) who wounds, the lion, and the snake. These are the causes contributing to death.
2
Classify each cause as hadar or non-hadar
Determine which causes have worldly legal consequence. According to the text, the lion's and snake's acts are hadar (legal void) in both this world and the Hereafter; the victim's self-harm is hadar in this world but sinful in the Hereafter; only the stranger's wound carries worldly liability.
Hadar means the act is legally null for purposes of diyah or penalty in this life.
3
Apply proportional attribution
Since the stranger's act is one of three effective 'genres' (self, stranger, animals), but the other two are hadar, the stranger bears only a proportional share. The share is one-third because there are three conceptually independent causal categories, but only the stranger's category produces liability.
The animals are treated as a single category because their acts are of one kind (hadar).
4
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the stranger pays one-third of the full diyah. This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah of Imam Muhammad, with no intra-Hanafi disagreement recorded.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Note the theological dimension
Self-harm and animal acts are hadar only in worldly law; they still have consequence in the Hereafter (e.g., the victim is sinful for self-harm). This distinguishes worldly liability from ultimate accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے اپنا سر زخمی کیا پھر دوسرے شخص نے اسی سر کو زخمی کیا پھر اسے سانپ نے کاٹ لیا پھر شیر نے اس پر حملہ کر دیا بالآخر وہ زخمی حالت میں مرگیا تو کیا دیت واجب ہے یا نہیں
قال ومن شج نفسه وشجه رجل وعقره اسد و اصابته حي فمات من ذلك كله فعلى الاجنبى ثلث الدية لان فعل الاسد والحية جنس واحد لكونه هدرا في الدنيا والاخرة وفعله بنفسه هدر في الدنيا معتبر في الاخرة حتى يوثم عليه
ترجمہ اور مد نے فرمایا کہ جس نے اپنا سر پھوڑا اور کسی شخص نے اس کا سر پھوڑا اور شیر نے اس کو پھاڑا اور سانپ نے اس کو ڈسا پس وہ ان تمام چیزوں کی وجہ سے مر گیا تواجنبی پر تہائی دیت ہے اس لئے کہ شیر اور سانپ کا فعل جنس واحد ہے اس کے رائیگاں ہونے کی وجہ سے دنیا اور آخرت میں اور اس کا ذاتی فعل دنیا میں ہدر آخرت میں معتبر ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ اس پر گنہگار ہوگا
تشریح زید نے خود اپنا سر پھوڑ لیا اور خالد نے بھی اس کا سر پھوڑا اور شیر نے زید کو پھاڑا اور سانپ نے اس کو ڈسا ان تمام اسباب کی وجہ سے وہ مر گیا تو خالد پر کتنی دیت واجب ہوگی ؟ تو فرمایا کہ تہائی دیت خالد پر واجب ہوگی کیونکہ گویا تین اسباب کی وجہ سے وہ مرا ہے اور
A person wounded his own head, then another person wounded the same head, then a snake bit him, then a lion attacked him; ultimately he died in that wounded state. Is diyah wajib or not? He said: Whoever wounds his own head, and a man wounds him, and a lion mauls him, and a snake bites him, and he dies from all of that, then upon the stranger (ajnabi) is one-third of the diyah. Because the act of the lion and the snake are of one kind, being wasted (hadar) in this world and the Hereafter, and his own act is wasted in this world but considered in the Hereafter so that he sins for it. Translation: And Muhammad said: Whoever wounds his own head, and someone wounds his head, and a lion mauls him, and a snake bites him, and he dies from all of these, then upon the stranger (the other person) is one-third of diyah. Because the acts of lion and snake are of one kind, being wasted in this world and the Hereafter, and his own act is wasted in this world but considered in the Hereafter, so that he is sinful for it. Commentary: Zaid wounded his own head, and Khalid also wounded his head, and a lion mauled Zaid, and a snake bit him. He died from all these causes. How much diyah is upon Khalid? He said: one-third diyah is upon Khalid, because as if he died from three causes.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is a ruling on when multiple causes contribute to death. The case: a person wounds himself, another person wounds him, a lion attacks, and a snake bites – all together cause death. The question: is diyah due, and on whom? The ruling from Imam Muhammad (as transmitted by al-Quduri? Actually the text says 'Mad'? 'قال ومن شج نفسه...' – likely from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan). The liability: the stranger (the other person who wounded) owes one-third of the full diyah. Why only one-third? The legal reasoning: The lion and snake acts are of one kind – they have no legal consequence in this world or the Hereafter (their actions are 'hadar' – wasted). The person's own self-wounding is also wasted in this world (no diyah for self-harm) but he is sinful in the Hereafter. The only effective cause with worldly liability is the wound by the stranger. However, since death is attributed to all three causes collectively (self, stranger, animals), the stranger's share is one-third. The animals' actions and self-harm do not produce diyah, so the stranger pays only his proportional share (1/3). The commentary clarifies by counting three causes: self, stranger, and animals (as a single genus).

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Legally inconsequential; no worldly liability.
اجنبی (ajnabī): The person other than the victim who caused injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for imposing only one-third diyah on the stranger when multiple causes contribute to death?
A) The stranger's wound was minor compared to others.
B) The self-harm and animal attacks are considered hadar (legally inconsequential) in worldly matters.
C) The stranger was not the sole cause of death.
D) The victim's heirs agreed to accept one-third.

Key Takeaway
When multiple causes of death include acts that are hadar (worldly inconsequential), the only effective cause among them bears a proportional share of diyah.

Dividing Diyah by Legal Genres of Actions
Explaining proportional diyah via talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why only one-third of the diyah is due from Khalid when multiple agents cause death, using the Hanafi classification of actions as hadar (void) or mu'tabar (considered) in this world and the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Liability in collective death is proportional to the legal genre of each action, not the physical contribution.

This passage addresses a question that arises when a death is caused by multiple agents with different legal capacities. How should the blood money (diyah) be divided? The Hanafi answer depends not on physical causation but on the legal classification of each agent's action. Actions are categorized by their consequence in this world and the Hereafter, and each distinct category (jins) bears an equal share of the liability. Understanding this principle requires us to examine the underlying reasoning (ta'lil) that the author provides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage to determine who the agents are (lion, snake, Zayd, Khalid) and what the question is: why is Khalid liable for only one-third of the diyah?
The scenario assumes all agents contributed to the death, but their legal status differs.
2
Classify Each Action by Legal Status
Determine for each action whether it is considered (mu'tabar) or inconsequential (hadar) in this world and the Hereafter. The lion and snake have no liability in either world → their actions are entirely hadar. Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter (he becomes sinful) but not in this world → partially considered. Khalid's action is considered in both worlds → fully considered.
The term 'hadar' means an action with no legal or spiritual consequence.
3
Count the Distinct Genres (Ajnas)
Group actions by their legal status. The lion and snake share the same status (both hadar) → count as one genre. Zayd's partial status is unique → second genre. Khalid's full status is unique → third genre. Thus three genres in total.
The classification is based solely on legal consequence, not physical similarity.
4
Apply Proportional Liability
Since the death resulted from three actions of three distinct genres, each genre is responsible for one-third of the destruction. Therefore, Khalid, representing one genre, owes one-third of the diyah.
This is a form of qiyas: the illa (effective cause) is the legal classification.
5
Evidence for Zayd's Partial Consideration
The author supports the claim that Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter by citing the scholarly dispute over washing and praying over a suicide. The existence of ikhtilaf shows the action is not completely void.
The suicide's action is analogous to Zayd's: both involve intentional self-harm, and the ruling on funeral prayer indicates some consequence in the Hereafter.

Source Text

سوال خالد کا فعل سبب کا ثلث کیسے ہے؟

كتاب الجنايات
جواب ... اس لئے شیر اور سانپ کا نفعل جنس واحد ہونے کی وجہ سے ایک فعل ہو گیا اور ایک فعل خودزید کا اور ایک فعل خالد کا تو خالد کانفعل سبب کا ثلث ہوا۔
سوال شیر اور سانپ کا فعل ایک جنس کیوں ہے اور ان دونوں کا الگ الگ کیوں ہے؟ جواب شیر اور سانپ کا فعل دنیا اور آخرت میں ہدر ہے یعنی نہ یہاں شیر اور سانپ کی گرفت ہوگی اور آخرت میں تو یہ دونوں تو جنس واحد ہو گئے اور زید کا فعل آخرت میں معتبر ہو گا دنیا میں ہر اور خالد کا فعل دنیا اور آخرت میں معتبر ہے اس لئے زید کا فعل نہ شیر اور سانپ سے ملحق ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ خالد کے فعل سے لہذا خالد کا فعل جملہ افعال کا ثلث ہوا تو اس پر ٹکٹ دیت واجب کر دی جائے گی۔
سوال . اس کی کیا دلیل ہے کہ زید کا فعل آخرت میں معتبر ہے؟ جواب ... زید اس کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوتا ہے اور اس گناہ کی وجہ سے مشائخ میں یہ اختلاف ہو گیا کہ اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی یا نہیں اور یہ اس کے ائم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے لہذا فر ماتے ہیں۔
اقوال فقہاء
وفى النوادران عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد يغسل ويصلى عليه وعندابي يوسف يغسل ولا يصلى عليه وفي شرح السير الكبير ذكر فى الصلوة عليه اختلاف المشايخ على ما كتبناه في كتاب التجنيس والمزيد ترجمہ اور نوادر میں ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک غسل دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی اور شیر کبیر کی شرح میں اس پر نماز پڑھنے کے بارے میں مشائخ کا اختلاف مذکور ہے جس کو ہم نے کتاب الجنیس والمزید میں لکھ دیا ہے۔ تشریح طرفین فرماتے ہیں کہ خود کشی کرنے والے پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور غسل دیا جائیگا اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک صرف غسل دیا جائے گا اور امانیہ نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ سیر کبیر کی شرح میں نماز کے بارے میں اختلاف مشائخ مذکور ہے جس کو مصنف نے اپنی کتاب والتجنيس والمزيد میں بیان کر دیا ہے مفتی بہ قول یہ ہے کہ نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور غسل دیا جائے گا۔ تفصیل کے لئے ملاحظہ ہوشا می ص ۵۸۴ ج ۱ اجنبی کا فعل دنیا و آخرت میں معتبر ہے
فلم یکن هدرا مطلقا وكان جنسا أخر وفعل الا جنبي معتبر في الدنيا والاخرة فصارت ثلثة اجناس فكان النفس تلفت بثلثة افعال فيكون التالف يفعل كل واحد ثلثة فيجب عليه ثلث الدية والله اعلم ترجمہ پس نہیں ہو گا ( زید کا نعل ) مطلقا رائیگاں اور وہ دوسری جنس ہوگا اور اجنبی کا فعل دنیا اور آخرت میں معتبر ہے تو سارے افعال تین جنس ہوئے پس گویا کہ نفس تین افعال سے تلف ہوا ہے تو ہر فعل سے تلف ہونے والا اس کا ثلث ہوا تو اس پر دیت کا ثلث واجب گا۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح زید کا فعل چونکہ من وجہ معتبر اور من وجہ ہدر ہے تو اس کو الگ ہی شمار کرنا پڑے گا لہذا سارے افعال تین جنس کے جمع ہو گئے اور خالہ کا فعل ان الفاظ کا ثلث ہے تو ثلث ہی اس پر دیت واجب ہوگی۔
Khalid's action is one-third of the causes, so the diyah will also be one-third.
Question: How is Khalid's action one-third of the cause?
Answer: Because the actions of the lion and the snake, being of one type, became one action; and one action is Zayd's own; and one action is Khalid's. So Khalid's action is one-third of the cause.
Question: Why are the actions of the lion and the snake of one type, and why are these two separate? Answer: The actions of the lion and the snake are inconsequential (hadar) in this world and the Hereafter, meaning there is no liability upon the lion or snake in this world, and in the Hereafter they are of one type. Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter, but in this world it is [partially] inconsequential. Khalid's action is considered in both this world and the Hereafter. Therefore, Zayd's action can neither be joined to the lion and snake nor to Khalid's action. Hence, Khalid's action is one-third of all actions, so one-third of the diyah is due upon him.
Question: What is the proof that Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter? Answer: Because Zayd becomes sinful due to it, and due to this sin the scholars have differed on whether funeral prayer should be performed over him or not, and this is because of his being a Muslim. Hence they say:
Statements of Jurists:
In al-Nawadir: According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, he is washed and prayed over; according to Abu Yusuf, he is washed but not prayed over. In Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, the difference of the scholars about prayer is mentioned, which we have written in Kitab al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. Translation: In al-Nawadir, it is stated that according to the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) he is given a bath and the funeral prayer is performed, while according to Abu Yusuf he is given a bath but not prayed over. In Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, the difference of the scholars regarding prayer is mentioned, as we have written in Kitab al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. Explanation: The two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) say that the one who commits suicide should be prayed over and given a bath; according to Abu Yusuf, only a bath is given, and the funeral prayer is not performed. In Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, the difference of the scholars regarding prayer is mentioned, which the author has stated in his book Kitab al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion is that the prayer should be performed and a bath given. For details, see footnote page 584 volume 1. The action of a stranger is considered in this world and the Hereafter.
So it (Zayd's action) was not absolutely inconsequential, and it became a separate genre. The action of the stranger is considered in this world and the Hereafter, so there are three genres. Thus, the life was destroyed by three actions, so the destruction caused by each action is one-third, so one-third of the diyah is due upon him. And Allah knows best. Translation: So it (Zayd's action) was not absolutely wasted, and it became a second genre. The stranger's action is considered in this world and the Hereafter, so all actions became three genres. So it is as if the life was destroyed by three actions, so the destruction per each action is one-third, so one-third of the diyah is due upon him. And Allah knows best. Explanation: Since Zayd's action is in one respect considered and in another respect inconsequential, it must be counted separately. Thus, all actions become three genres, and Khalid's action is one-third of these actions, so one-third of the diyah is due upon him.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) concerning the division of diyah when multiple agents contribute to a death. The scenario involves Zayd, a lion, a snake, and Khalid. The author explains why Khalid is liable for one-third of the diyah. The key principle is that actions are classified into genres based on their legal consequences in this world and the Hereafter. The actions of the lion and the snake are 'hader' (void) in both worlds, so they count as one genre. Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter (he becomes sinful) but not in this world (no liability), so it is a separate genre. Khalid's action is considered in both worlds, so it is a third genre. Thus, the life is destroyed by three actions of three different genres, and each action is responsible for one-third of the destruction, so Khalid pays one-third of the diyah. The author then supports the claim that Zayd's action is considered in the Hereafter by citing the difference of opinion among scholars regarding washing and praying over a suicide. The narration from al-Nawadir states that according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, the suicide is washed and prayed over, while Abu Yusuf says only washed, not prayed over. The mufta bihi opinion is to wash and pray. This dispute is evidence that Zayd's action is not completely void, as it has consequence in the Hereafter. The passage then repeats the Arabic text that summarizes the legal conclusion: three genres, each responsible for one-third, so one-third diyah.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money, a financial compensation paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of wrongful death.
هدر (hadar): Void, inconsequential; an action for which there is no legal or spiritual consequence in this world or the Hereafter.
جنس (jins): Genre, category; here it refers to a class of actions that share the same legal status regarding consequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the actions of the lion and snake count as a single genre?
A) They are both animals.
B) Their actions are completely void (hadar) in both worlds.
C) They acted together in the same incident.
D) They are not responsible for their actions.

Key Takeaway
When multiple agents cause death, Hanafi fiqh divides diyah proportionally based on the number of distinct legal genres (ajnas) among the contributing actions, not on physical causation.

Ruling on One-Third Diyah When Three Acts Cause Death
Explains division of diyah when three independent acts cause death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when three independent acts cause death and explain the basis for proportional liability.

Core Idea
When three acts cause death, each actor pays one-third diyah — liability is proportional to causation.

This passage addresses a specific case of multiple causation in homicide. The Hanafi school holds that when three independent acts, each from a different person, contribute to a death, each actor is liable for one-third of the full diyah. This ruling is based on the principle that liability is proportional to causation, and each act is treated as an independent cause of one-third of the death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
There are three independent acts, each from a different person, combining to cause a single death. No single act is the sole cause.
The acts must be independent and each contributory.
2
State the ruling
Each actor is liable for one-third of the full diyah.
The diyah is divided equally among the number of independent causal acts.
3
Understand the reasoning
The ruling rests on the principle that liability is proportional to causation. Each act is considered to have caused one-third of the death.
If the acts were not independent (e.g., sequential), the ruling may differ.
4
Apply the ruling
In any case with multiple independent causes of death, diyah is divided equally among the number of contributors.
This applies to unintentional and quasi-intentional killings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تین جنس ہوئے پس گویا کہ نفس تین افعال سے تلف ہوا ہے تو ہر فعل سے تلف ہونے والا اس کا ثلث ہوا تو اس پر دیت کا ثلث واجب گا۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح زید کا فعل چونکہ من وجہ معتبر اور من وجہ ہدر ہے تو اس کو الگ ہی شمار کرنا پڑے گا لہذا سارے افعال تین جنس کے جمع ہو گئے اور خالہ کا فعل ان الفاظ کا ثلث ہے تو ثلث ہی اس پر دیت واجب ہوگی۔
Three types occurred, so it is as if the life was destroyed by three acts, so for each act the destroyed part is its third, so one-third of the diyah is obligatory upon him. And Allah knows best. Commentary: Zaid's act is valid from one aspect and wasted from another, so it must be counted separately; hence all acts are collected into three types, and the aunt's act is one-third of these words, so only one-third diyah is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage states a Hanafi ruling on multiple causation in homicide. When three independent acts, each from a different person, contribute to a single death, each actor is liable for one-third of the full diyah. The commentary explains that acts are counted separately, and only the proportion directly attributed to each is required. This is based on the principle that liability is proportional to causation. The ruling applies to cases where the acts are not clearly predominant or wholly wasted; the share of diyah is divided accordingly.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation paid to the heirs of the victim in cases of homicide (except when qiṣāṣ applies).
ثلث (thuluth): One-third share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) One-third diyah
D) No diyah

Key Takeaway
Liability for diyah is divided equally among the number of independent causal acts.

Obligation to Kill the Weapon-Brandisher
Ruling and proof for killing a weapon-brandisher.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a person who brandishes a weapon against Muslims and explain the three proofs supporting the obligation.

Core Idea
Whoever brandishes a weapon against Muslims forfeits his inviolability; it is wajib to kill him.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's works establishes a critical ruling on self-defense and communal protection. When a person, even if a Muslim, threatens Muslims with a weapon, the community is obligated to kill him. The ruling is derived from a prophetic hadith, the concept of rebellion (baghy), and the necessity of repelling harm. We will examine the proofs and the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is brandishing a weapon (sword) against Muslims. The ruling is that it is wajib to kill that person.
Wajib means obligatory, not merely permissible.
2
Analyze the first proof: Hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever brandishes a sword against Muslims, his blood is made permissible.' This shows the blood is wasted (dam hadar).
The hadith is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli).
3
Examine the second proof: Rebellion
The person is a rebel (baghi), and rebellion removes inviolability ('ismah) according to Hanafi principles.
Even if the person is a Muslim, rebellion against the community forfeits protection.
4
Understand the third proof: Self-defense
Killing is the prescribed means to repel death from oneself; thus it is permissible and obligatory to defend.
This is based on the principle of necessity (darurah).
5
Identify the obligation indicator
The phrasing 'upon them to kill him' and 'it is the right of Muslims to kill him' both indicate wujub.
Imam Muhammad uses 'فعليهم' and 'ف حق على المسلمين' to denote obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسلمان پر تلوار سونتنے والے سے قتل کا حکم
قال ومن شهر على المسلمين سيفا فعليهم ان يقتلوه لقوله علية السلام من شهر على المسلمين سيفا فقد اطل دمه ولا نه باغ فتسقط عصمته ببغيه ولا نه تعين طريقا لدفع القتل عن نفسه فله قتله ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اور جس نے مسلمانوں پر تلوار سونت لی تو مسلمانوں پر واجب ہے کہ اس کو قتل کریں نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ جس نے مسلمانوں پر تلوار سونت لی پس اس نے اپنا خون رائیگاں کر دیا اور اس لئے کہ وہ باقی ہے تو اس کی بغاوت کی وجہ سے اس کی عصمت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور اس لئے کہ قتل ہی معین طریقہ ہے اپنے نفس سے قتل کی مدافعت کیلئے تو مسلمان کیلئے اس کا قتل جائز ہوگا۔ تشریح جو شخص اگر چہ مسلمان ہو مسلمانوں پر تلوار سونت لے تو مسلمانوں پر واجب ہے کہ اس کو قتل کر دیں کیونکہ اس حدیث کے مطابق جو مذکور ہوئی ہے اس کی عصمت ساقط ہو گئی اور اس کا خون رائیگاں ہو گیا ہے نیز یہ باغی ہے اور بغاوت عصمت کو ختم کر دینے والی ہے نیز اگر اس کو قتل نہ کیا جائے تو اپنے نفس سے مدافعت مشکل ہے تو اب مدافعت کا طریقہ صرف قتل ہے لہذا قتل کا جواز ثابت ہو گیا۔ امام محمد کی دو عبارتوں سے اشارہ ہے کہ قتل کرنا واجب ہے وقوله فعليهم وقول محمد فى الجامع الصغير فحق على المسلمين ان يقتلوه اشارة الى الوجوب والمغنى وجوب دفع الضرر ترجمہ اور محمد کا قول فعلیہم اور محمد کا قول جامع صغیر میں پس حق ہے مسلمانوں پر کہ اس کوقتل کر میں وجوب کی جانب اشارہ ہے اور وجہ ضرر کے دور کرنے کا وجوب ہے تشریح امام محمد نے مبسوط میں فعلیھم فرمایا ہے اور جامع صغیر میں یوں فرمایا ہے فحق على المسلمين ان يقتلوه ان دونوں عبارتوں سے یہ بات معلوم ہوئی ہے کہ قتل کرنا واجب ہے اور وجوب اس لئے ہے تا کہ اپنے نفس سے ضر کو دور کر سکے ( وفی اقوال اخر ) مسلمان پر تلوار یا ہتھیار سونت لے تو دوسرے کو کیا کرنا چاہئے آبادی کے اندر ہو یا باہر ، دن اور رات میں فرق کا حکم وفي سرقة الجامع الصغير ومن شهر على رجل سلاحا ليلا او نهارا او شهر عليه عصا ليلا في مصر ونهارا في طريق في غير مصر فقتله المشهور عليه عمدا فلا شئ عليه لما بين ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر کی کتاب السرقہ میں ہے اور جس نے کسی شخص پر ہتھیار سونتا رات میں یا دن میں یا اس پر لاٹھی سونتی رات کو شہر میں یا دن میں ایسے راستہ میں جو شہر میں نہیں ہے پس اس کو مشہور علیہ نے (جس پر تلوار سونی گئی تھی ) عد اقتل کر دیا تو اس پر کوئی شئی نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح کسی شخص نے کسی پر ہتھیا رسونت لیا دن ہو یا رات ہو یا لٹھ سنبھال لیا اور شہر میں سنبھالا لیکن رات میں یا دن میں سنبھالا کہیں جنگل میں پس یہ پوزیشن دیکھ کر جس پر ہتھیار یاتھ سونا گیا تھا اس نے سونے والے کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر کوئی منمان ہوگا اس سابق حدیث کی وجہ ہے۔ قاتل پر عدم قصاص کی وجہ وهذا لان السلاح لا يلبث فيحتاج الى دفعه بالقتل والعصا الصغيرة وان كان يلبث ولكن في الليل لا يلحقه الغوث فيضطر الى دفعه بالقتل وكذا فى النهار فى غير المصر فى الطريق لا يلحقه الغوث فاذا قتله كان دمه هدرا قالا فان كان عصالا تلبث يحتمل ان يكون مثل السلاح عندهما ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ ہتھیار نہیں ٹھہر تا پس وہ مشہور عالیہ ) اس کی مدافعت کا محتاج ہو گا قتل کے ذریعہ اور چھوٹی لاٹھی اگر چہ ٹھہرتی ہے اور رات میں اس کو فریا درس نہیں پہنچے گا تو وہ قتل کے ذریعہ اس کی مدافعت کا محتاج ہو گا اور ایسے ہی دن میں شہر سے باہر راستہ میں اس کو فریا درس نہیں پہنچے گا۔ پس جب اس نے (مشہور علیہ نے ) اس کو ( مشاہر کو قتل کر دیا تو اس کا خون رائیگاں ہو گا مشائخ نے فرمایا پس اگر ایسا لٹھ ہو جو نہ ٹھہرے تو احتمال ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ ہتھیار کے مثل ہو جائے ۔ تشریح جو جامع صغیر میں قیودات لگائی گئی ہیں، یہاں سے مصنف ان کی وجہ بیان کرتے ہیں :۔ ہتھیار دن میں ہو یا رات میں سب کا حکم یکساں ہے کیونکہ ہتھیار تو فورا اپنا کام کرے گا تو یہاں یہ اپنی جان بچانے کے لئے قتل کرنے پر بہر صورت مجبور ہے۔ - اگر سونے والے نے لٹھ سونتا ہے تو اس کے لئے رات اور جنگل کی قید لگائی ہے رات کی قید اس لئے کہ لٹھا اگرچہ فورا عموما نہیں مارتا مگر رات میں کوئی حمایتی اس کو نہیں مل سکے گا جو اس کو چھڑا سکے اور ایسے ہی دن میں اگر جنگل میں ہو وہاں بھی کوئی چھڑانے والا نہیں مل سکے گا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں بھی اس کو مجبور شمار کیا جائے گا اور یوں سمجھیں گے کہ جیسے وہ پہلی صورت میں مجبور تھا اب بھی مجبور ہے لہذا اگر اس نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ ماقبل میں مسئلہ گزر چکا ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک لٹھ ہتھیار کے درجہ میں ہے لہذا ان کے نزدیک اللھ یہاں بھی ہتھیار کے درجہ میں ہوگا اور مشکل ہتھیار اگر اس نے اٹھے سونتا تو رات اور دن شہر اور جنگل کا حکم یکساں ہوگا۔
Ruling on killing the one who brandishes a sword against Muslims. He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever brandishes a sword against Muslims, it is upon them to kill him, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever brandishes a sword against Muslims, his blood has been made permissible.' And because he is a rebel, so his inviolability falls due to his rebellion. And because it is a specified way to repel death from oneself, so it is permissible for him to kill him. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: ... Commentary: The obligation to kill is established from the hadith and the need to repel harm. And his saying 'upon them' and his saying in al-Jami' al-Saghir 'it is the right of Muslims to kill him' indicates obligation. Further, in the Book of Theft of al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever brandishes a weapon against a man by night or day, or brandishes a stick by night in a town or by day on a road outside a town, and the one at whom it was brandished kills him intentionally, there is nothing upon him for the reason explained. Commentary: The defender is compelled and no liability attaches. And this is because a weapon does not wait, so he needs to repel it by killing. A small stick, even if it waits, but at night no helper reaches him, so he is compelled to kill; likewise in the day on a road outside the town no helper reaches him. So when he kills him, his blood is wasted. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If it is a stick that does not wait, it is probable that it is like a weapon according to them. Commentary: The author explains the conditions in al-Jami' al-Saghir: For a weapon, day and night are the same because it acts immediately. For a stick, the restriction of night and desert is because help is not available, so the defender is compelled. The earlier discussion stated that according to the Sahibayn, a stick is like a weapon, so the same rule applies.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the obligation to kill a person who brandishes a weapon against Muslims. The proof is the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared such a person's blood to be wasted (i.e., his sanctity is forfeited). The ruling is based on three reasons: (1) the hadith, (2) the fact that the person is a rebel (baghi) and thus loses his inviolability, and (3) the necessity of self-defense: killing is the specified means to repel the threat. The passage also addresses details from al-Jami' al-Saghir: if the aggressor uses a weapon, the defender may kill him anytime (day or night, town or desert) and faces no liability. If the aggressor uses a stick, the defender may kill him without liability only when help is unavailable: at night in a town, or during the day on a road outside a town. The reason is that a weapon causes immediate harm, whereas a stick may not, so the defender's necessity is conditioned on the inability to get help. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) add that if the stick is of a type that does not wait (i.e., is as dangerous as a weapon), it is treated like a weapon. The author then summarizes that for weapons, day/night and town/desert make no difference; for sticks, the conditions of night and desert apply. This ruling falls under the category of defensive killing, not punitive execution, and the authority is from the Zahir al-Riwayah works of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
شهر عليه سلاحا (shahara 'alayhi silāḥan): To brandish a weapon against someone in a threatening manner.
عصمة (‘iṣmah): Inviolability or sanctity that protects a person's life and property.
بغى (baghā): Rebellion or transgression against legitimate authority; here refers to the aggressor's unjustified attack.
دم هدر (damun hadarun): Blood that is wasted, i.e., killing such a person does not entail any liability or punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is the status of a person who brandishes a sword against Muslims?
A) His blood is protected
B) His blood is wasted
C) He must be imprisoned
D) He must be fined

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates killing a person who brandishes a weapon against Muslims due to the hadith, the loss of inviolability through rebellion, and the necessity of self-defense.

Conditions for Killing the Aggressor: Weapon vs. Stick
Detailed conditions for permissible killing without liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for a weapon and a stick when killing an aggressor, and identify the conditions that make the killing permissible without liability.

Core Idea
A weapon always permits killing; a stick permits it only when help is unavailable.

Imam Muhammad's detailed discussion in al-Jami' al-Saghir specifies when killing an aggressor is free from liability. The key distinction is between a weapon, which acts immediately, and a stick, which may not. The defender's necessity is evaluated based on the availability of help. We will explore these conditions and the Sahibayn's supplementary opinion.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for a weapon
For a weapon (sword, gun, etc.), day or night, town or desert, the defender may kill the aggressor without liability because the weapon does not wait.
The weapon can kill instantly, so the defender is always compelled.
2
State the rule for a stick
For a stick, killing without liability is only allowed at night in a town or by day on a road outside a town, because help is not available.
If help is available, the defender should seek help and not kill.
3
Explain the reasoning
The stick may not cause immediate death, so the defender is only compelled when he cannot get help. If help is available, he should seek it instead of killing.
This is based on the principle of repelling harm with the least harmful means.
4
Note the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if the stick is of a type that does not wait (i.e., it can kill as quickly as a weapon), it is treated like a weapon.
This expands the scope: any dangerous stick is like a weapon.
5
Summarize the practical outcome
The mufta bihi is that the conditions for a stick stand, but the Sahibayn's view is also considered for sticks that are equally dangerous.
In practice, a judge may evaluate the stick's danger.

کرتے ہیں :۔ ہتھیار دن میں ہو یا رات میں سب کا حکم یکساں ہے کیونکہ ہتھیار تو فورا اپنا کام کرے گا تو یہاں یہ اپنی جان بچانے کے لئے قتل کرنے پر بہر صورت مجبور ہے۔ - اگر سونے والے نے لٹھ سونتا ہے تو اس کے لئے رات اور جنگل کی قید لگائی ہے رات کی قید اس لئے کہ لٹھا اگرچہ فورا عموما نہیں مارتا مگر رات میں کوئی حمایتی اس کو نہیں مل سکے گا جو اس کو چھڑا سکے اور ایسے ہی دن میں اگر جنگل میں ہو وہاں بھی کوئی چھڑانے والا نہیں مل سکے گا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں بھی اس کو مجبور شمار کیا جائے گا اور یوں سمجھیں گے کہ جیسے وہ پہلی صورت میں مجبور تھا اب بھی مجبور ہے لہذا اگر اس نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ ماقبل میں مسئلہ گزر چکا ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک لٹھ ہتھیار کے درجہ میں ہے لہذا ان کے نزدیک اللھ یہاں بھی ہتھیار کے درجہ میں ہوگا اور مشکل ہتھیار اگر اس نے اٹھے سونتا تو رات اور دن شہر اور جنگل کا حکم یکساں ہوگا۔
Ruling on killing the one who brandishes a sword against Muslims. He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever brandishes a sword against Muslims, it is upon them to kill him, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever brandishes a sword against Muslims, his blood has been made permissible.' And because he is a rebel, so his inviolability falls due to his rebellion. And because it is a specified way to repel death from oneself, so it is permissible for him to kill him. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: ... Commentary: The obligation to kill is established from the hadith and the need to repel harm. And his saying 'upon them' and his saying in al-Jami' al-Saghir 'it is the right of Muslims to kill him' indicates obligation. Further, in the Book of Theft of al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever brandishes a weapon against a man by night or day, or brandishes a stick by night in a town or by day on a road outside a town, and the one at whom it was brandished kills him intentionally, there is nothing upon him for the reason explained. Commentary: The defender is compelled and no liability attaches. And this is because a weapon does not wait, so he needs to repel it by killing. A small stick, even if it waits, but at night no helper reaches him, so he is compelled to kill; likewise in the day on a road outside the town no helper reaches him. So when he kills him, his blood is wasted. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If it is a stick that does not wait, it is probable that it is like a weapon according to them. Commentary: The author explains the conditions in al-Jami' al-Saghir: For a weapon, day and night are the same because it acts immediately. For a stick, the restriction of night and desert is because help is not available, so the defender is compelled. The earlier discussion stated that according to the Sahibayn, a stick is like a weapon, so the same rule applies.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the obligation to kill a person who brandishes a weapon against Muslims. The proof is the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared such a person's blood to be wasted (i.e., his sanctity is forfeited). The ruling is based on three reasons: (1) the hadith, (2) the fact that the person is a rebel (baghi) and thus loses his inviolability, and (3) the necessity of self-defense: killing is the specified means to repel the threat. The passage also addresses details from al-Jami' al-Saghir: if the aggressor uses a weapon, the defender may kill him anytime (day or night, town or desert) and faces no liability. If the aggressor uses a stick, the defender may kill him without liability only when help is unavailable: at night in a town, or during the day on a road outside a town. The reason is that a weapon causes immediate harm, whereas a stick may not, so the defender's necessity is conditioned on the inability to get help. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) add that if the stick is of a type that does not wait (i.e., is as dangerous as a weapon), it is treated like a weapon. The author then summarizes that for weapons, day/night and town/desert make no difference; for sticks, the conditions of night and desert apply. This ruling falls under the category of defensive killing, not punitive execution, and the authority is from the Zahir al-Riwayah works of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
شهر عليه سلاحا (shahara 'alayhi silāḥan): To brandish a weapon against someone in a threatening manner.
عصمة (‘iṣmah): Inviolability or sanctity that protects a person's life and property.
بغى (baghā): Rebellion or transgression against legitimate authority; here refers to the aggressor's unjustified attack.
دم هدر (damun hadarun): Blood that is wasted, i.e., killing such a person does not entail any liability or punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir, when is killing a person who brandishes a stick permissible without liability?
A) Any time, just like a weapon
B) Only at night in a town or by day on a road outside a town
C) Only during the day in a town
D) Only if the stick is made of metal

Key Takeaway
The defender is only liable for killing an aggressor with a stick when help is available; otherwise the blood is wasted.

Liability When the Aggressor is a Madman, Child, or Animal
Inter-madhhab dispute on liability with intra-Hanafi distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a madman or child brandishes a weapon, and explain why the Hanafi school requires diyah while the Shafi'i school does not.

Core Idea
Defender must pay diyah even if the aggressor is a madman, because inviolability is not forfeited by an act lacking legal capacity.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on whether self-defense against a legally incompetent aggressor exempts the defender from liability. The Hanafi school, following Imam Muhammad, holds that the defender must pay diyah (blood money) when killing a madman or child who brandishes a weapon, because their act does not forfeit their inviolability. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering the aggressor's act legally null, so no liability attaches. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi distinction for animals from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Imam Muhammad: if a madman brandishes a weapon and is killed, the defender must pay diyah from his own property. The same applies to a child.
Diyah is wajib in intentional killing when qiṣāṣ is not applicable.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no liability attaches because the madman's act is legally irrelevant; the defender is excused.
The Shafi'i view considers the madman's aggression as null, so self-defense is fully justified.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf distinguishes: for an animal, he says compensation (ḍamān) is obligatory, but not for a child (or madman? — text cuts off). Imam Muhammad's position is that all three cases (madman, child, animal) follow the same rule as the madman.
The text ends abruptly; the dominant Hanafi view for animals is that the defender pays the animal's value unless it was dangerous.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the defender pays diyah (or ḍamān for animal); under Shafi'i, the defender pays nothing.
This affects whether the defender must compensate the family of the deceased or the owner of the animal.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school follows Imam Muhammad for madman and child (diyah), and for animals, the more detailed ruling (based on other texts) is that the defender pays the animal's value unless the animal was inherently dangerous (e.g., a wolf or guard dog).
Abu Yusuf's opinion on animals is often preferred in later Hanafi fatawa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان شهر المجنون على غيره سلاحا فقتله المشهور عليه عمدا فعليه الدية فى ما له وقال الشافعي لا شيء عليه و على هذا الخلاف الصبى والدابة وعن ابى يوسف انه يجب الضمان في الدابة ولا يجب في
He said: And if a madman brandishes a weapon against another person, and the one at whom it was brandished kills him intentionally, then diyah is due from his property. Al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is due upon him. And on this disagreement is the child and the animal. And from Abu Yusuf: indeed, compensation (ḍamān) is obligatory for the animal, and is not obligatory in [the case of the child?].
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. It discusses the ruling when a legally incompetent person (madman, child) or an animal brandishes a weapon and is killed by the defender. According to the text (attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), if a madman brandishes a weapon and the defender kills him intentionally, the defender must pay diyah from his own property. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no liability attaches because the madman's act is not a legal aggression. The same disagreement applies to a child and an animal. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: for an animal, he says compensation (ḍamān) is obligatory (presumably on the defender), but it is not obligatory in the case of a child (or madman?) — the text cuts off. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the defender is liable for diyah when the aggressor is a madman or a child, but for an animal, the defender is liable for its value (ḍamān) unless the animal was dangerous. This is because the act of a madman or child is not a valid aggression that forfeits their inviolability, so the defender's killing is considered a direct killing of a protected person, requiring diyah. In contrast, Shafi'i considers the madman's act as null, so the defender is not liable. The passage highlights the practical difference: in the Hanafi view, the defender must pay diyah; in the Shafi'i view, he pays nothing.

Key Terms
مجنون (majnūn): A person who is insane or mentally incompetent, lacking legal responsibility (taklīf).
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of homicide (except qiṣāṣ).
ضمان (ḍamān): Compensation or guarantee; here refers to monetary liability for the value of the animal killed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a madman brandishes a weapon and the defender kills him, what is the ruling?
A) No liability
B) Qisas
C) Diyah from the defender's property
D) Ta'zir

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, killing a madman or child aggressor in self-defense does not exempt the defender from paying diyah, because their inviolability remains intact.

Self-defense when attacker brandishes a weapon
Ruling with proof on no liability for killing a brandishing attacker

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which killing an attacker brandishing a weapon or stick incurs no liability (diyah or qisas) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Killing a weapon-brandishing attacker is permissible without liability if no help is available.

This lesson examines a ruling from Jami' al-Saghir regarding self-defense when someone brandishes a weapon or a stick. The text clarifies when the defender's lethal response results in no financial or penal liability. We will analyze the conditions for this ruling and the reasoning behind treating a stick differently based on time and location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being judged (killing the brandisher) and the hukm (ruling) — here, no liability (hadar al-dam).
The ruling applies when the defender kills the attacker who brandishes a weapon or a stick under specific conditions.
2
Locate the conditions for the ruling
List the conditions that must be present: weapon brandished (any time/place) or stick brandished (night in city, or day outside city).
The condition 'no help available' (ghauth) is key for the stick scenario.
3
Trace the reasoning (talil)
Understand why the ruling differs for a weapon vs. a stick: a weapon strikes immediately, while a stick may be slower. For a stick, the absence of help (night/desert) creates necessity (darurah) for lethal defense.
This reasoning is based on the principle that necessity justifies killing when no other recourse exists.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Observe that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) consider a stick that does not delay (i.e., strikes quickly) as equivalent to a weapon in all cases.
This means under their view, the conditions of night/desert may not be needed for a quick stick.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
Identify the relied-upon ruling for fatwa: no liability in the specified cases, with the Sahibayn's view extending the weapon ruling to quick sticks.
The text from Jami' al-Saghir is considered zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر کی کتاب السرقہ میں ہے اور جس نے کسی شخص پر ہتھیار سونتا رات میں یا دن میں یا اس پر لاٹھی سونتی رات کو شہر میں یا دن میں ایسے راستہ میں جو شہر میں نہیں ہے پس اس کو مشہور علیہ نے (جس پر تلوار سونی گئی تھی ) عد اقتل کر دیا تو اس پر کوئی شئی نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح کسی شخص نے کسی پر ہتھیا رسونت لیا دن ہو یا رات ہو یا لٹھ سنبھال لیا اور شہر میں سنبھالا لیکن رات میں یا دن میں سنبھالا کہیں جنگل میں پس یہ پوزیشن دیکھ کر جس پر ہتھیار یاتھ سونا گیا تھا اس نے سونے والے کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر کوئی منمان ہوگا اس سابق حدیث کی وجہ ہے۔
قاتل پر عدم قصاص کی وجہ
وهذا لان السلاح لا يلبث فيحتاج الى دفعه بالقتل والعصا الصغيرة وان كان يلبث ولكن في الليل لا يلحقه الغوث فيضطر الى دفعه بالقتل وكذا فى النهار فى غير المصر فى الطريق لا يلحقه الغوث فاذا قتله كان دمه هدرا قالا فان كان عصالا تلبث يحتمل ان يكون مثل السلاح عندهما ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ ہتھیار نہیں ٹھہر تا پس وہ مشہور عالیہ ) اس کی مدافعت کا محتاج ہو گا قتل کے ذریعہ اور چھوٹی لاٹھی اگر چہ ٹھہرتی ہے اور رات میں اس کو فریا درس نہیں پہنچے گا تو وہ قتل کے ذریعہ اس کی مدافعت کا محتاج ہو گا اور ایسے ہی دن میں شہر سے باہر راستہ میں اس کو فریا درس نہیں پہنچے گا۔ پس جب اس نے (مشہور علیہ نے ) اس کو ( مشاہر کو قتل کر دیا تو اس کا خون رائیگاں ہو گا مشائخ نے فرمایا پس اگر ایسا لٹھ ہو جو نہ ٹھہرے تو احتمال ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ ہتھیار کے مثل ہو جائے ۔
Translation: And in Jami' al-Saghir's book of al-Sarqah it is said: Whoever brandishes a weapon against a person at night or during the day, or brandishes a stick at night in the city or during the day on a road that is not within the city, then the one at whom it was brandished kills him, nothing is owed due to the evidence we have mentioned. Explanation: If a person brandishes a weapon against another, day or night, or grabs a stick in the city at night or during the day in a desert, seeing this situation, the one at whom the weapon was brandished kills the brandisher, then no compensation is required because of the previous hadith. Reason for no retaliation on the killer: This is because the weapon does not delay [in striking], so he needs to repel it by killing. As for a small stick, even if it delays, at night he will not receive help, so he is compelled to repel it by killing. Likewise, during the day outside the city on a road, he will not receive help. So if he kills him, his blood is shed in vain. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If the stick does not delay, it is probable that it is like a weapon in their view.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding self-defense when someone brandishes a weapon or a stick. The ruling is taken from Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad. The text states that if a person draws a sword (or any weapon) against another, whether day or night, and the targeted person kills the attacker in self-defense, there is no liability (no qisas or diyah). The same applies if a stick is brandished at night in the city or during the day outside the city (in a desert or wilderness). The reason provided is that a weapon strikes immediately, so the defender is compelled to kill to save himself. A stick may not strike immediately, but at night in the city or during the day in a desert, no help is available, so the defender is similarly compelled. The commentary adds that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if the stick is such that it does not delay (i.e., is like a weapon in its speed), it is treated like a weapon in all cases. This ruling is based on a hadith mentioned earlier (the text references 'the previous hadith'). The principle is that necessity (darurah) justifies killing in self-defense when there is no other way to repel the attack.

Key Terms
شهر السلاح (shahr al-silah): Brandishing a weapon in a threatening manner against someone.
هدر الدم (hadar al-dam): Blood shed with no liability (no qisas or diyah).
الغوث (al-ghauth): Help or rescue that may arrive to prevent the killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qisas is obligatory.
B) Diyah is due on the killer's family.
C) No liability (blood is shed in vain).
D) The killer must pay compensation (diyah) from his own wealth.

Key Takeaway
Killing an attacker who brandishes a weapon or a stick is without liability only when the defender has no other recourse and no help is available, with specific conditions for a stick (night in city or day outside city).
