Self-defense against insane, child, or animal attacker
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah when attacker is non-responsible (child, insane) or animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when killing a child or insane attacker in self-defense, and explain how Abu Yusuf's view on animal attackers differs.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, killing a child or insane attacker requires diyah, but killing an animal does not—because their inviolability differs.

This passage from Jami' al-Saghir presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on self-defense. While self-defense generally justifies killing an adult brandisher without liability, the ruling changes when the attacker is a child, insane, or animal. Understanding why diyah is due here reveals the Hanafi principles of inviolability (isma) and legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
What is the ruling when a person kills an insane, child, or animal attacker in self-defense? The passage addresses whether diyah is due.
2
State the position of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad rules in Jami' al-Saghir that diyah is due from the killer's wealth for killing an insane or child attacker. The same ruling applies to animals.
The phrase 'عليه الدية في ما له' indicates a financial obligation.
3
Contrast with Imam al-Shafi'i's view
Al-Shafi'i holds no diyah is due, analogizing to an adult brandisher and arguing the killer is like one coerced.
This is an inter-madhhab difference.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's distinction
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between animal and child/insane: for an animal, the owner pays compensation; for child/insane, no diyah from the killer.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
5
Analyze the reasoning
The child and insane have partial legal capacity; their actions are considered, and their inviolability is personal. The animal has no capacity; its inviolability belongs to its owner. Thus, killing a child/insane invokes diyah, while killing an animal invokes compensation to the owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان شهر المجنون على غيره سلاحا فقتله المشهور عليه عمدا فعليه الدية فى ما له وقال الشافعي لا شنی عليه و على هذا الخلاف الصبى والدابة وعن ابى يوسف انه يجب الضمان في الدابة ولا يجب في الصبى والمجنون للشافعى انه قتله دافعا عن نفسه فيعتبر بالبالغ الشاهر ولا نه يصير محمولا على قتله بفعله فاشبه المكره
ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور اگر مجنون نے اپنے غیر پر ہتھیار سونت لیا پس مشہور علیہ نے اس کو عمد اقتل کر دیا تو قاتل پر اس کے مال میں دیت واجب ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاتل پر کچھ نہیں ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر بچہ اور چوپایہ ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ چوپایہ میں منعمان واجب ہے اور بچہ اور مجنون میں واجب نہیں ہے۔ شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاتل نے اس کو اپنے نفس کی جانب سے مدافعت کی عرض سے قتل کیا ہے تو اس کو شاہر بالغ پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور اس لئے کہ قاتل مقتول کے قتل کے فعل سے ابھارا گیا ہے تو قاتل مکرہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔
ولابي يوسف ان فعل الدابة غير معتبر اصلاحتى لو تحقق لا يوجب الضمان اما فعلهما معتبر حتى لو حققاه يجب عليهما الضمان وكذا عصمتهما لحقهما وعصمة الدابة لحق ما لكها فكان فعلهما مسقطا للعصمه دون فعل الدابة
Translation: Muhammad said in Jami' al-Saghir: If an insane person brandishes a weapon against another, and the one at whom it was brandished kills him intentionally, then he owes diyah from his wealth. Al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is owed upon him. And on this disagreement is the child and the animal. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the guarantee is obligatory for the animal, but not obligatory for the child and the insane. For al-Shafi'i, his evidence is that the killer killed him defending himself, so it is analogized to the adult brandisher; also because the killer is incited to kill by the victim's action, so he resembles the one who is coerced (mukrah). And for Abu Yusuf: The action of the animal is not considered at all, even if it occurs, it does not necessitate guarantee. But the action of these two (child and insane) is considered in a general sense, so that if they actualize it, guarantee is obligatory upon them. Likewise, their inviolability (isma) is due to their own right, while the inviolability of the animal is due to the right of its owner. Therefore, their action becomes a cause for dropping inviolability, unlike the action of the animal.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding self-defense when the attacker is an insane person, a child, or an animal. The ruling from Imam Muhammad (recorded in Jami' al-Saghir) is that if an insane person brandishes a weapon, and the targeted person kills him intentionally, the killer must pay diyah from his own wealth. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no compensation is due at all. The text then notes that the same difference applies to a child and an animal (though Abu Yusuf distinguishes between them). Abu Yusuf's view is that if the attacker is an animal, the guarantor (owner) must pay compensation (the value of the animal), but if the attacker is a child or insane person, no compensation is due from the killer. The reasoning: Shafi'i analogizes to an adult brandisher (who would not be entitled to diyah if killed in self-defense) and also argues that the killer is like one coerced (mukrah) because the victim's action provoked the killing. Abu Yusuf argues that the action of an animal has no legal consequence (it is not responsible), whereas the actions of a child and insane person are partially considered; they have their own inviolability, so killing them requires diyah, unlike an animal whose inviolability is based on its owner's property right.

Key Terms
المجنون (al-majnun): An insane person who lacks legal capacity.
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
الدابة (al-dabbah): An animal (beast of burden).
الدية (al-diyah): Blood money paid in compensation for homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as stated in Jami' al-Saghir, what is the ruling if an insane person brandishes a sword and the targeted person kills him intentionally?
A) No liability, as the insane person is not responsible.
B) The killer must pay diyah from his own wealth.
C) The killer receives qisas.
D) The killer must pay half diyah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the inviolability of a child or insane person is not dropped by their aggression; thus diyah is due in self-defense, unlike for a sane adult attacker.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Liability for Killing a Child or Madman Attacker
Intra-Hanafi dispute about killing a child/madman attacker

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liability for killing a child or madman attacker and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A child's attack does not remove his inviolability — diyah is wajib because he lacks sound choice.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability when a person kills a child or madman who is attacking him. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the act of the child/madman has some legal validity, thereby removing his inviolability and absolving the killer of compensation. Imam Abu Hanifa, whose view is relied upon, holds that because the child/madman lacks sound choice, his act cannot remove his inviolability, so diyah is obligatory. This dispute revolves around the concept of ismah and the role of sound choice in legal accountability.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
The core legal question: Is diyah wajib upon a person who kills a child or madman attacking him? State both Abu Hanifa's view (diyah wajib) and Abu Yusuf's view (no liability).
Note that the child's ismah is at stake.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between an animal (act has no validity) and a child/madman (act has some validity). Since the child's act has validity, it removes his own ismah, so no compensation is due.
He argues the child's act is legally considered, e.g., if a child kills someone, diyah is due from his property.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof (lana)
Abu Hanifa holds that both the animal and the child/madman lack sound choice (ikhtiyar sahih). Without sound choice, an act cannot remove ismah. Therefore, the child's ismah remains, and killing him requires compensation.
The fact that qisas is not obligatory on the child for killing another proves lack of sound choice.
4
Examine the response to the objection
A reader objects: if Abu Hanifa considers the child's act invalid, why is qisas not wajib on the killer? The answer: because the killer had a permissible excuse (mubih) — repelling evil. This prevents qisas but does not negate monetary liability (diyah).
Thus the killer repays compensation despite being excused from criminal qisas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf's view, the killer owes nothing; under Abu Hanifa's, the killer must pay diyah. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa.
Zahir al-Riwayah supports Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text

و لنا انه قتل شخصا معصوما او اتلف ما لا معصوما حقا للمالك وفعل الدابة لا يصلح مسقطا وكذا فعلهما و ان كانت عصمتهما حقهما لعدم اختيار صحيح ولهذا لا يجب القصاص بتحقق الفعل منهما بخلاف العاقل البالغ لان له اختيارا صحيحا وانما لا يجب القصاص لوجود المبيح وهو دفع الشر فتجب الدية

تشریح یہ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں دیت اور ضمان قیمت واجب ہے کیونکہ اول صورت میں قاتل نے معصوم الدم شخص کو قتل کیا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں ایسا مال تلف کیا ہے جو حق مالک کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے۔ اور اے ابو یوسف یہ کیا فرمایا کہ چوپایہ کا فعل مسقط عصمت نہیں اور مجنون اور بچہ کافضل عصمت کو ساقط کرنے والا ہے۔ یہ صحیح نہیں جبکہ دونوں کا فعل غیر مستقط ہے چوپایہ کا تو ظاہر ہے اور مجنون اور بچہ کا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں اختیار صحیح نہیں ہے اور اختیار صحیح نہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر بچہ اور مجنون کسی کو قتل کر دیں تو قصاص واجب نہیں ہوگا وہ دوسری بات ہے کہ ان دونوں کی عصمت اپنا حق ہے اور چوپایہ کی عصمت حق مالک کی وجہ سے ہے لیکن اختیار صحیح نہ ہونے میں سب برابر ہیں ۔ اور رہا بالغ جس نے تلوار سونت لی تھی اور اس کو قتل کر دیا گیا تھا تو قاتل پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوا تھا کیونکہ اس بالغ میں اختیار صحیح موجود ہے۔

سوال جب بچہ اور مجنون کی صورت میں امام صاحب نے دیت واجب کی ہے یعنی ان کے فعل کو غیر معتبر شمار کر لیا ہے پھر تو قاتل پر بجائے دیت کے قصاص واجب ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب بھی ہاں بات تو یونہی ہونی چاہئے مگر یہاں قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قاتل نے خوامخواہ قتل نہیں کیا بلکہ ایک نیچ اس کے حق میں موجود ہے اور وہ اس کے شر کو دور کرنا ہے اس میسج کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے دیت واجب ہوگئی اور قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf, the summary of which is that there is a difference between an animal and a madman or child: the act of an animal is not considered valid, but the act of a child and madman is considered valid in some respects. The second difference is that the inviolability of a madman and child is inherent to them and is their right, while the inviolability of an animal is not inherent but due to the right of its owner. When this difference is clear, then the act of an animal is in the category of non-existence, so the animal's inviolability is not removed by its act, and when inviolability is not removed, then killing it necessitates guarantee of its value. And because the act of a child and madman is considered valid in some respects, their inviolability is deemed removed by their act. And when inviolability is removed, then no compensation is due for killing them. The proof that their act is considered valid is that if they kill someone, they become liable for compensation. However, due to not being legally responsible, qisas is not obligatory upon them.

And for us: He killed an inviolable person or destroyed property inviolable by the right of the owner. The act of an animal is not suitable to remove inviolability, and similarly their act, even if their inviolability is their right, due to lack of sound choice. For this reason, qisas is not obligatory despite the actual act from them, unlike a sane adult because he has sound choice. And qisas is not obligatory due to the existence of a permissible excuse, which is repelling evil, so diyah becomes obligatory.

Explanation: This is the proof of the two parties (the other side): that in all these cases diyah and guarantee of value are obligatory because in the first case the killer killed an inviolable person, and in the second case he destroyed property that is inviolable due to the right of the owner. And O Abu Yusuf, what you said that the act of an animal does not remove inviolability but the act of a madman and child does remove it—this is not correct, since the act of both is not fit to remove inviolability: that of an animal is apparent and that of a madman and child because they do not have sound choice. The proof that they lack sound choice is that if a child or madman kills someone, qisas is not obligatory. That is a separate matter that their inviolability is their right while the inviolability of an animal is due to the right of the owner, but in lacking sound choice they are all equal. As for the adult who brandished a sword and was killed, the killer was not liable because that adult had sound choice.

Question: When Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) has made diyah obligatory in the case of a child and madman, meaning he considered their act invalid, then should qisas be obligatory on the killer instead of diyah? Answer: Yes, that would be the case, but here qisas will not be obligatory because the killer did not kill without reason; rather, there is an excuse on his part, which is repelling evil. Due to the presence of this permissible excuse, diyah becomes obligatory and qisas does not.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Abu Hanifa (referred to as Imam Sahib) regarding the liability of a person who kills a child or madman who is attacking him. The passage first explains Abu Yusuf's position, then gives the opposing view of Abu Hanifa and the majority, and then answers a potential objection. Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes between an animal's act (which has no legal validity) and the act of a child or madman (which has some validity). Therefore, if one kills an animal that attacks, compensation is due; but if one kills a child or madman who attacks, no compensation is due because their own act removed their inviolability. The opposing view (attributed to the majority of the madhhab, including Abu Hanifa) argues that neither the act of an animal nor that of a child/madman can remove inviolability because they lack sound choice (ikhtiyar sahih). Therefore, regardless of who attacks, killing an inviolable person or property requires compensation (diyah or guarantee of value). The question arises: If Abu Hanifa considers the child/madman's act invalid, then why is diyah due instead of qisas? The answer is that the killer had a valid excuse (repelling evil), which prevents qisas but does not eliminate the need for monetary compensation. This dispute revolves around the concept of ismah (inviolability) and the effect of a person's act in removing it, particularly when the actor lacks full legal capacity.

Key Terms
عصمت (ismah): Inviolability or sanctity of life and property that protects from being violated without legal justification.
اختیار صحیح (ikhtiyar sahih): Sound choice or volition that qualifies a person for full legal capacity and accountability.
مبیح (mubih): A permissible excuse that allows an otherwise prohibited act, such as repelling evil in self-defense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is due upon a person who kills a child who attacks him with a weapon?
A) Nothing, because the child's own act removed his inviolability.
B) Qisas, because the child is inviolable.
C) Diyah (blood money), because the child's act does not remove inviolability and the killer had an excuse.
D) Both qisas and diyah.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa's view that diyah is wajib when killing a child/madman attacker is mufta bihi because lack of sound choice prevents removal of ismah, while the mubih only removes qisas, not financial liability.

Ruling on Killing a Retreating Attacker: Qisas Required
Ruling with proof about qisas when a retreating attacker is killed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a retreating attacker and explain why retreat restores inviolability, mandating qisas.

Core Idea
Once the attacker retreats, his inviolability returns; killing him becomes murder requiring qisas.

This lesson examines a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Hidayah. The scenario: a person draws a weapon, strikes another, then retreats. A third party then kills the retreating attacker. The ruling clarifies that the retreat restores the attacker's inviolability (ismah), so the killing is unjustified and qisas is obligatory. This principle underscores the temporary nature of a muharib's loss of protection, which ends once aggression ceases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing a person who had previously attacked and then retreated. The ruling: qisas (retaliatory execution) is due upon the killer.
The ruling applies only after clear retreat; the attacker is no longer a muharib.
2
Locate the legal basis
Imam Muhammad states: 'He drew a weapon... then another kills him, then qisas is due.' The basis is the talil: 'because he left being a muharib by turning away, so his inviolability returned.'
This is a direct textual proof from a Zahir al-Riwayah source.
3
Analyze the key concept: muharib and insiraf
A muharib loses inviolability only during active aggression. 'Insiraf' (turning away) indicates the cessation of the attack, which restores ismah. Without ongoing threat, killing becomes murder.
The Hanafi school emphasizes that the status is tied to overt behavior, not mere intent.
4
Confirm the absence of ikhtilaf
This ruling is affirmed in Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon across schools (muttafaq alayh). There is no intra-Hanafi dispute on this specific point.
Unanimity reinforces the ruling's reliability for fatwa.
5
Apply to variations
If the retreat is feigned or the attacker pauses only to resume attack, the insiraf is not genuine. The critical factor is the clear cessation of the threat.
This aligns with the broader principle: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' — intentions matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شهر على غيره سلاحا فى المصر فضربه ثم قتله الاخر فعلى القاتل القصاص معناه اذا ضربه صرف لانه خرج من ان يكون محارباً بالانصراف فعادت عصمته

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے غیر پر شہر میں ہتھیار کھینچ لیا پس اس کو مارا پھر اس کو دوسرے نے قتل کر دیا تو قاتل پر قصاص واجب ہوگا اس کے معنی یہ ہیں جب کہ اس کو مارا ہو پس لوٹ گیا اس لئے کہ وہ انصراف کی وجہ سے محارب ہونے سے خارج ہو گیا تو اس کی عصمت لوٹ آئی۔

تشریح زید نے خالد پر شہر میں ہتھیار کھینچا پھر خالد کو مثلاً ایک دو مار کر چلا آیا یعنی اب دوبارہ مارنے کا ارادہ نہیں رہا۔ اب خالد نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو خالد پر قصاص واجب ہوگا کیونکہ جب زید چلا آیا تو اب وہ محارب نہیں رہا۔ تو اب وہ معصوم الدَم ہے اور معصوم الدم کے قبل سے قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever draws a weapon against another in the city and strikes him, then another person kills him (the first), then qisas is due upon the killer. Its meaning is when he struck him and then turned away, because he left being a muharib by turning away, so his inviolability returned.

Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever draws a weapon against another in the city and strikes him, then another kills him, then qisas is due upon the killer. Its meaning is when he struck him and then turned back, because he left being a muharib by turning away, so his inviolability returned.

Explanation: Zayd drew a weapon against Khalid in the city, then struck Khalid once or twice and left, meaning he no longer intended to strike again. Now Khalid killed him, so qisas is due upon Khalid because when Zayd left, he was no longer a muharib. Thus he is now inviolable, and killing an inviolable person necessitates qisas.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This is a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in the matn of al-Hidayah. It addresses a scenario where a person (Zayd) draws a weapon in a city, strikes the victim (Khalid), then retreats (either by walking away or ceasing the attack). A third person (or possibly Khalid himself) then kills Zayd. The ruling is that qisas is obligatory upon the killer because after Zayd retreated, he ceased to be a muharib (one who is lawfully killed due to aggression). His inviolability (ismah) returned. Therefore, killing him after the retreat is murder without justification, mandating qisas. The commentary clarifies that the retreat must be a clear disengagement from the attack, indicating no further intent to harm. This ruling distinguishes between attacking during the act of aggression (where killing the attacker may be permissible as self-defense or to prevent harm) and after the aggression has ceased.

Key Terms
محارب (muharib): One who draws a weapon with intent to kill or harm, thus losing his inviolability temporarily.
انصراف (insiraf): Turning away or retreating from the attack, indicating the cessation of aggression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zayd draws a sword on Khalid in the city, strikes him once, and then walks away, and Khalid then kills Zayd, what is the ruling?
A) Khalid is exempt from any liability because Zayd attacked him.
B) Khalid must pay diyah only.
C) Qisas is obligatory upon Khalid because Zayd's retreat restored his inviolability.
D) Khalid must pay half diyah.

Key Takeaway
A retreating attacker's inviolability is restored, making his subsequent killing murder subject to qisas.

Permissibility of Killing a Night Thief to Recover Property
Ruling with proof about killing a night thief when recovering property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a night thief when recovering property, and explain the conditions and proof for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Killing a night thief to retrieve property incurs no liability when recovery is impossible without it.

Imam Muhammad clarifies a crucial case: when a thief enters at night, steals, and flees, the owner who kills him while pursuing is not liable. The ruling is based on the hadith 'قاتل دون مالک' and extends the principle of defense to recovery. But the key condition is necessity—recovery must be impossible except by killing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing a thief who entered at night, stole property, and fled. The ruling is permissibility (mubah) with no liability (no diyah or qisas) for the owner.
Liabilities normally apply for killing, but here they are waived.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the prophetic hadith 'قاتل دون مالک' (Fight for your wealth). It is a hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut but with clear guidance.
The imperative form (قاتل) indicates permission to fight, even to kill, for property.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly commands fighting for wealth, implying that defending property by force is permissible. The Hanafi school extends this from initial defense (دفع) during the theft to recovery (استرداد) after the theft, as long as necessity persists.
The extension is based on qiyas: both situations share the same need to protect property.
4
Note the conditions
The ruling is conditional: (1) the theft must occur at night, (2) the owner must be unable to recover the property except by killing the thief.
If either condition is missing, the killing may incur liability. Daytime theft or alternative recovery methods would change the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن دخل عليه غيره ليلا واخرج السرقة فاتبعه وقتله فلا شئى عليه لقوله عليه السلام قاتل دون مالک ولانه يباح له القتل دفعا فى الابتداء فكذا استرداد ا فى الانتهاء وتاويل المسألة اذا كان لا يتمكن من الاسترداد الا بالقتل والله اعلم

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس پر رات میں اس کا غیر داخل ہوا اور اس نے چوری کا مال نکالا پس اپنے (مسروق منہ نے ) اس کا پیچھا کیا اور اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر کوئی شئی کو جب نہیں ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ اپنے مال کے پیچھے قتال کر اور اس لئے کہ اس کے لئے ابتداء ہی میں مدافعت کی وجہ سے قتل مباح ہے تو ایسے ہی انتہاء میں واپس لینے کے لئے (مباح ہے ) اور مسئلہ کی تاویل جب کہ وہ واپس لینے پر قدرت نہ رکھے مگر قتل ہی کی وجہ سے۔ واللہ اعلم

تشریح کسی شخص کے گھر میں چور گھسا اور مال مسروق کو باہر نکال کر بھا گا گھر والے نے اس کا پیچھا کیا اور چور کوقتل کر دیا تو گھر والے پر کوئی سنمان نہ ہوگا کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ قاتل دون مالک یعنی اپنے مال کی وجہ سے قتال کرو۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever has someone enter upon him at night and takes out stolen property, then he follows him and kills him, then there is nothing upon him due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Fight for your wealth.' And because killing is permissible for him in defense at the beginning, so similarly for recovery at the end. The interpretation of the case is when he cannot recover the property except by killing. And Allah knows best.

Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever has someone enter upon him at night and takes out stolen property, then the owner follows him and kills him, then there is no liability upon him because of the Prophet's hadith: 'Fight for your wealth.' And because killing is permissible for him in defense initially, so similarly it is permissible for recovery at the end. The interpretation of the case is when he cannot recover the property except by killing. And Allah knows best.

Explanation: When a thief enters a person's house at night and takes out stolen property and flees, and the owner follows and kills him, then there is no liability upon the owner because the hadith says: 'Fight for your wealth.'
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This is another ruling from Imam Muhammad. It deals with a night thief who enters a house, takes property, and runs away. The owner chases him and kills him. According to this ruling, the owner incurs no liability (no diyah or qisas) provided that he could not recover his property except by killing the thief. The proof is the hadith 'قاتل دون مالک' (fight for your wealth), which indicates that defending one's property even by killing is permissible when necessary. The ruling extends the permission from initial defense (during the theft) to recovery (after the theft), as long as there is no other means to retrieve the property. The commentary adds that this is conditional upon the inability to recover by other means. This ruling falls under the category of دفاع (defense) of property.

Key Terms
دفع (daf'): Defense or repelling an attacker; here it refers to defending property by killing the thief if necessary.
استرداد (istirdad): Recovery or retrieval of stolen property from the thief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, under what condition is it permissible to kill a thief who has stolen property at night and fled?
A) Always, because the thief is mubah al-dam.
B) Only if the thief resists arrest.
C) Only if the owner cannot recover the property except by killing the thief.
D) Only if the theft was committed in a city.

Key Takeaway
Killing a night thief in pursuit is permissible without liability only when recovery of property is impossible except by killing.

Non-Fatal Injuries: No Shibh 'Amd
Ruling with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of non-fatal injuries and explain why shibh 'amd is inapplicable using the tool-based rationale.

Core Idea
Non-fatal injuries are only intentional or accidental; quasi-intent exists only in homicide.

In Hanafi criminal law, injuries that do not result in death (ma dun al-nafs) are treated differently from homicide. While homicide can be classified as intentional ('amd), quasi-intentional (shibh 'amd), or accidental (khata'), non-fatal injuries are only either intentional or accidental. This passage from al-Quduri, explained by later commentators, provides the key reasoning: quasi-intent hinges on the tool's nature, which affects the outcome of killing but not of non-fatal harm. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying qisas and diyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal categories
List the three categories of harm: 'amd (intentional), shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional), and khata' (accidental). Note that the passage claims only two apply below life.
2
Understand the author's claim
Al-Quduri states: 'There is no shibh 'amd below life; it is either 'amd or khata'.' This is the core ruling.
3
Locate the proof (dalil aqli)
The proof is a rational argument: shibh 'amd pertains to the tool because killing varies with the tool (a sword kills more surely than a stick). However, for non-fatal injuries, the outcome (e.g., a broken bone) does not vary with the tool—any tool can cause the same injury.
This is a qiyas-style reasoning: the illa (tool variation) is absent in non-fatal injuries.
4
Note the thamarah (practical consequence)
Since there is no shibh 'amd, the diyah (blood money) for non-fatal injuries is either full if intentional or reduced if accidental. No intermediate category exists for penalties.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab dispute
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may extend shibh 'amd to maiming. The Hanafi position restricts it to homicide, as explained in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وليس فيما دون النفس شبه عمد انما هو عمد او خطأ لان شبه العمد يعود الى الالة والقتل هو الذى يختلف باختلافهما دون ما دون النفس لا نه لا يختلف اتلافه باختلاف الآلة فلم يبق الا العمد والخطا
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور نفس کے علاوہ میں شبہ عمد نہیں ہے وہ تو ( مادون النفس ) عمد یا خطاء ہے اس لئے کہ شبہ عمد آلہ کی جانب لوٹتا ہے اور قتل ہی آلہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے مختلف ہوتا ہے نہ کہ وہ جو نفس کے علاوہ ہے اس لئے کر ا دون انفس کا اختلاف آلہ کے اختلاف کی سے مختلف نہ ہوگا تو عمد اور خطاء کے علاوہ کوئی باقی نہ رہا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں ج ۵۲۶/۴ صفحہ پر تفصیل گزر چکی ہے کہ بہ عمر پورے قتل میں تو ہوسکتا ہے اعضاء کے تورات میں صرف روی صورتیں ہوں گی یا تو عمد یا خطاء جس کی وجہ ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔
He said: There is no shibh 'amd below the life; it is either 'amd or khata'. Because shibh 'amd returns to the tool, and killing is what differs by their difference, not that which is below the life, because its destruction does not differ by the difference of the tool. So nothing remains except 'amd and khata'. Translation: Al-Quduri said: There is no shibh 'amd in what is below life; it is either 'amd or khata'. Because shibh 'amd pertains to the tool, and killing varies by the variation of tools, but that which is below life does not vary in its destruction by the variation of tools. So only 'amd and khata' remain. Explanation: Previously, on page 526/4, detail has passed that in full killing, shibh 'amd can occur; in injuries to limbs, only 'amd or khata' are possible, the reason for which has passed previously.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage clarifies the categorization of non-fatal injuries. In Hanafi law, injuries that do not result in death (ma dun al-nafs) cannot be classified as shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional). Shibh 'amd is a category specific to homicide, where the intention is to injure but not kill, using a tool that is not likely to cause death. For bodily injuries below life, the classification is binary: either intentional ('amd) or accidental (khata'). The reason is that shibh 'amd depends on the nature of the tool used, which affects the outcome of killing but does not affect the outcome of a non-fatal injury— any tool can cause the same injury. Therefore, the only categories are 'amd (intentional, leading to qisas or diyah) and khata' (accidental, leading to diyah only).

Key Terms
ما دون النفس (ma dun al-nafs): Injuries that are not fatal; bodily harms below the level of taking life.
شبه عمد (shibh 'amd): Quasi-intentional act: one intends to hit but not to kill, using a tool unlikely to kill. Applies only to homicide.
عمد ('amd): Intentional act: the actor intends the act and the outcome, or intends an act that typically causes that outcome.
خطأ (khata'): Accidental act: no intent to harm; the outcome is unintended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is shibh 'amd not applicable to injuries below life?
A) Because the Quran does not mention it
B) Because the tool does not affect the outcome of non-fatal injuries
C) Because all such injuries are considered accidental
D) Because it is a later innovation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, non-fatal injuries are never shibh 'amd; they are always either intentional ('amd) or accidental (khata'), because the tool-based rationale for shibh 'amd is exclusive to homicide.

No Shabah Amd in Wounds Below the Soul
Ruling stating no quasi-intentional category for wounds below the soul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that shabah amd does not apply to injuries below the soul and explain the talil (reason) based on the instrument's relevance.

Core Idea
Shabah amd (quasi-intentional) is for homicide only; wounds are either intentional or accidental.

This passage clarifies an important limit on the category of quasi-intentional injury (shabah amd). In Hanafi law, shabah amd exists only for homicide, where the instrument may change the classification. For non-lethal injuries, the instrument is irrelevant: any intentional act causing harm is considered intentional, and any accidental act is accidental. Understanding this simplifies the classification of wounds and avoids an unnecessary intermediate category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first part of the passage: 'There is no quasi-intentional in what is below the soul; it is only intentional or accidental.' This is the core ruling.
The ruling is absolute – no shabah amd for ma dun al-nafs.
2
Identify the talil (reason)
The word 'لان' (because) introduces the reason: quasi-intentional relates to the instrument, and killing differs by instrument, but what is below the soul does not differ in its destruction by instrument.
The talil is based on the nature of the injury.
3
Understand the implication
Since the category of shabah amd depends on the instrument's typical lethality, and for non-lethal injuries the instrument does not change the legal result (any intentional harm is amd), the third category collapses. Thus, only 'amd and khata apply.
This is a distinctive Hanafi simplification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ليس فيما دون النفس شبه عمد انما هو عمد او خطأ لان شبه العمد يعود الى الالة والقتل هو الذى يختلف باختلافهما دون ما دون النفس لا نه لا يختلف اتلافه باختلاف الآلة فلم يبق الا العمد والخطا
And he said: There is no quasi-intentional (shabah amd) in what is below the soul; it is only intentional or accidental. Because quasi-intentional refers to the instrument, and killing is what differs by their difference, unlike what is below the soul, because its destruction does not differ by difference of instrument, so only intentional and accidental remain.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage clarifies that for injuries less than death (ma dun al-nafs), there is no intermediate category of shabah amd. In homicide, the instrument used determines whether it is 'amd (intentional) or shabah amd (quasi-intentional); but for wounds, the severity of injury does not depend on the instrument in the same way. Wounds are classified either as deliberate ('amd) or accidental (khata'), with no third category. This is a distinctive Hanafi position that simplifies the classification of non-lethal injuries.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shabah amd): Quasi-intentional killing where the instrument is not typically lethal
مادون النفس (ma dun al-nafs): Injuries that are less than fatal, i.e., wounds or loss of limbs

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which categories of injury exist for wounds below the soul (ma dun al-nafs) in Hanafi law?
A) Intentional, quasi-intentional, and accidental.
B) Intentional and quasi-intentional only.
C) Intentional and accidental only.
D) Quasi-intentional and accidental only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the category of quasi-intentional (shabah amd) only applies to homicide, not to injuries below the soul; such injuries are only intentional or accidental.

Victim's Choice When Offender's Hand Is Defective
Ruling on victim's option to take defective hand or full diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a victim in Hanafi law when the offender's hand is defective and explain the qiyas analogy that justifies the ruling.

Core Idea
When exact equality is impossible, the victim may choose either the defective hand or full diyah.

In cases of qisas for intentional injury, the Hanafi school requires equivalence between the victim's and offender's limbs. But what happens when the offender's hand is withered or missing fingers? This lesson examines the ruling from al-Hidayah and the qiyas analogy that gives the victim a choice between accepting a defective retaliation or claiming full blood-money.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the two options the victim has: cut the defective hand (qisas) and accept it as is, or forgo qisas and take full diyah.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi corpus.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to a case of destroyed fungible goods. The text explicitly parallels the two cases.
The analogy is based on the inability to exact the full right.
3
Analyze the qiyas analogy
Compare the original case (asl: destruction of a fungible item that becomes unavailable) with the new case (far': qisas with a defective hand). Identify the illa: ta'addhur istifa' al-haqq kamilan (inability to exact the full right).
The illa is jaliyyah (evident) and extracted via tanqih al-manat.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not permit qisas with a defective hand or may restrict the option, but the Hanafi school gives the victim full choice.
This lesson does not detail opposing views, but the status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Understand the consequence
Once the victim chooses either option and it is executed, his right is extinguished. This is likened to accepting inferior goods in satisfaction of a debt.
The victim’s consent to the defective hand waives any further claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵
ایک کا ہاتھ صحیح سالم ہے اور دوسرے کا شل ( خشک ) یا انگلیاں کم ہیں، تو قصاص لینے میں اور دیت لینے میں اختیار ہے
قال واذا كانت يد المقطوع صحيحة ويد القاطع شلاء او ناقصة الاصابع فالمقطوع بالخيار ان شاء قطع اليد المعيبة ولا شى له غيرها وان شاء اخذ الا رش كاملا لان استيفاء الحق كملا متعذر فله ان يتجوز بدون حقه وله ان يعدل الى العوض كا لمثلى اذا انصرم عن ايدى الناس بعد الاتلاف ثم اذا استوفاها ناقصا فقد رضى به فيسقط حقه كما اذا رضى بالردى مكان الجيد ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ کاٹا ہوا ہاتھ صحیح ہو اور کاٹنے والے کا ہاتھ خشک ہو یا ناقص الا صابع ہو تو جس کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا ہے اسے اختیار ہے کہ چاہے تو عیب دار ہاتھ کاٹ دے اور اس کے لئے اس عیب دار ہاتھ کے علاوہ کچھ نہیں ہے اور اگر چاہے تو ہاتھ کی پوری دیت لے، اس لئے کہ کامل حق کو وصول کرنا مستعد ر ہے تو مقطوع کے لئے حق ہے کہ وہ اپنے حق سے کم میں چشم پوشی کر لے اور اس کے لئے حق ہے کہ عوض ( دیت) کی طرف عدول کرے جیسے مثلی جب کہ وہ لوگوں کے ہاتھ سے اتلاف کے بعد ختم ہو جائے پھر جب مقطوع نے ناقص ہاتھ سے وصول کر لیا تو وہ اس سے راضی ہو گیا تو اس کا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا، جیسے جب وہ عمدہ کی جگہ ردی سے راضی ہو جائے۔ تشریح زید کا ہاتھ صحیح سالم ہے اور بکر کا ہاتھ شل ہے خشک ہے یا اس کی انگلیاں کم ہیں اور صورت یہ ہوئی کہ بکر نے زید کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا تو اب زید کیا کرے تو اس کو دو اختیار ہیں ۔ 1- اگر زید چاہے تو بکر کا ہاتھ جیسا بھی ہے ویسے ہی سے قصاص لے لے اور اس کو کاٹ دے کیونکہ جب کامل ہا تھ بکر کا ہے ہی نہیں تو اس کے علاوہ چارہ کار نہیں ہے اور اپنے حق سے کم پر راضی ہونا اور اسی حال پر چشم پوشی کر لینا جائز ہے اور اگر اس نے ایسا کر لیا تو اس کا حق ادا ہو گیا اور یہ ایسا ہو گا جیسے عمدہ درہم کی بجائے ردی لے لینا۔
-
-۲ نیز زید کو اختیار ہے کہ قصاص نہ لے بلکہ دیت لے لے۔ اور اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے کہ زید نے بکر کی کوئی مشکلی چیز ہلاک کر دی تو زید پر واجب تھا کہ اس کا مثل ادا کرے مگر اتفاق سے وہ چیز بازار میں نہیں ہے اور اگر ہے تو گھٹیا ہے تو اب بکر کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو جیسی بازار میں وہ چیز مل رہی ہے اس کو لینے پر راضی ہو جائے اور اس صورت میں اس کا حق ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر چاہے تو اس کی قیمت لے لے اسی طرح بالکل صورت مذکورہ میں ہے۔
Book of Injuries. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidaya, volume 15. A man has a sound hand and the other has a withered (dry) hand or missing fingers; so he has a choice in taking retaliation or blood-money. He (al-Quduri) said: If the hand of the person whose hand was cut is sound, and the hand of the cutter is withered or deficient in fingers, then the person whose hand was cut has a choice: if he wishes, he may cut the defective hand, and he has nothing else besides it; and if he wishes, he may take the full blood-money, because exacting the full right is impossible, so he has the option to be lenient regarding his right and also to turn to compensation, like the case of a fungible when it ceases to exist among people after destruction. Then when he recovers it deficiently, he has consented to it, so his right falls, just as when he accepts inferior goods in place of good ones. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When the cut hand is sound and the cutter's hand is dry or deficient in fingers, then the one whose hand was cut has a choice: if he wants, he cuts the defective hand and has nothing besides it; and if he wants, he takes the full blood-money of the hand, because receiving the complete right is impossible, so the person whose hand was cut has the right to overlook part of his right and to turn to the substitute (blood-money), like when a fungible after destruction disappears from people's hands. Then when he recovers it deficiently, he has consented to it, so his right falls, just as when he accepts inferior in place of good. Commentary: Zaid's hand is sound, and Bakr's hand is withered or has missing fingers, and the situation is that Bakr cut Zaid's hand. Now what does Zaid do? He has two options: 1. If Zaid wants, he can take retaliation from Bakr's hand as it is, and cut it, because since Bakr does not have a complete hand, there is no alternative, and being content with less than one's right is permissible. If he does so, his right is fulfilled, and this is like taking inferior dirhams in place of good ones. 2. Also, Zaid has the option not to take retaliation but rather to take blood-money. Its example is exactly like if Zaid destroyed a fungible item of Bakr's; then it was obligatory upon Zaid to return its equivalent, but by chance that item is not available in the market, or if it is, it is inferior. Then Bakr has the choice: if he wants, he accepts what is available in the market, and in that case his right is fulfilled; and if he wants, he takes its price. This is exactly the same as the mentioned case.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on qisas (retaliation) when the offender's hand is defective (shalla, withered, or missing fingers). The author states that the victim has a clear choice: either cut the defective hand of the offender in qisas, accepting it as it is with no further compensation, or forgo qisas and claim the full diyah (blood-money). The rationale given is that since it is impossible to exact the full right (i.e., cutting a sound hand equivalent to the victim's), the victim may either accept less in kind or seek monetary compensation. The analogy (qiyas) is drawn from a case of destruction of fungible property: if the exact replacement is unavailable or defective, the owner may take the available defective item or claim its value. This ruling is established in Zahir al-Riwayah, and the victim's consent to the defective hand extinguishes his right, just as accepting inferior goods satisfies a debt.

Key Terms
ید شلاء (yad shalla'): A hand that is withered, dry, or paralyzed, considered defective.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injury, prescribed for intentional assault.
دية (diyah): Monetary compensation paid to the victim or heirs for bodily harm or death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two options available to a victim when the offender's hand is defective (shalla) and the victim's hand is sound?
A) The victim must take the defective hand in qisas and nothing else.
B) The victim may either cut the defective hand and forgo further compensation, or take full diyah.
C) The victim can only demand diyah, since qisas is not possible.
D) The victim can demand double diyah because the offender has a defect.

Key Takeaway
When perfect equality in qisas is impossible, the victim may choose between accepting a defective retaliation or claiming full diyah.

6 min
Ruling When Defective Hand Is Lost Before Choice
Ruling on loss of defective hand before victim's election.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a defective hand is lost before the victim elects qisas or diyah, and identify the exception when the hand was cut for a legal right.

Core Idea
If the defective hand is destroyed before choice, both claims are lost except if cut for a legal right.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in jinayat where the offender's defective hand (ma'ufa) is destroyed before the victim exercises his option between qisas and diyah. The Hanafi school rules that the victim loses both claims, with a subtle exception when the hand was cut in execution of a legal penalty. Understanding this ruling reveals how the school fixes a right initially to the person of the offender and only permits transfer to property upon explicit election.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the initial right
The act is a wrongful amputation (jinaya) against the victim. The victim's right is initially fixed to qisas (retaliation) on the corresponding limb of the offender.
The right is tied to the specific limb, not a property substitute.
2
Determine the condition for transfer to diyah
Transfer to diyah (blood money) occurs only when the victim explicitly chooses it. Without that choice, diyah is not yet due.
The choice is an active election, not a default option.
3
Apply the ruling to loss of the limb before choice
If the offender's defective hand is destroyed (falls by itself or is cut unjustly by a third party) before the victim chooses diyah, then both qisas (locus absent) and diyah (not yet elected) are lost.
The victim gets nothing.
4
Distinguish the exception
If the hand was cut as a legal penalty (qisas for another crime or hadd for theft), diyah is still obligatory because the hand is considered 'sound in meaning'—the state's action vindicated a right.
The exception preserves the diyah claim despite the hand's loss.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that nothing is due in the main case, and the exception confirms the principle.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf reported; the position is consistent across the school.

سالم رہا۔
تشریح بکر کا وہ ہاتھ جس کا ذکر چل رہا تھا خود بخود گر گیا یا ظلما کسی نے کاٹ دیا تو اب کیا ہوگا؟ مجنی علیہ سے زید مراد ہے جس کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا ہے۔
تو بہر حال اگر زید نے ابھی دیت لینا اختیار نہ کیا ہو بلکہ ابھی اس کا ذکر ہی نہیں آیا تھا یا زید نے قصاص کو منتخب کر لیا تھا کہ یہ صورت پیش آگئی کہ بکر کے ہاتھ کو کسی نے ظلماً کاٹ دیا یاوہ خود ہی گر گیا تو اب نہ قصاص رہا اور نہ دیت کیونکہ واجب اصلی تو یہاں قصاص ہے اور مال جب واجب ہوتا ہے کہ مجنی علیہ دیت کو اختیار کرے۔ حالانکہ اس صورت میں مجنی علیہ نے دیت کو اختیار نہیں کیا لہذا نہ قصاص ہوگا اور نہ دیت، قصاص اس لئے نہ ہوگا کہ محل قصاص ندارد ہے اور دیت اس لئے نہیں کہ اس کو اختیار نہیں کیا گیا تھا۔ البتہ اگر مجنی علیہ دیت لینا اختیار کر چکا تھا اور یہ واقعہ پیش آیا ہو تو دیت کا وجوب برقرار ہے۔ اور یہی تمام صورتیں ہیں لیکن اس کا ہا تھ ظلما نہیں کاٹا گیا بلکہ کسی حق کے بدلہ میں کاٹا گیا ہے جو اس پر واجب ہے مثلاً قصاص میں کاٹا گیا ہے یا چوری میں کاٹا گیا ہے تو اب کسی بھی صورت میں مجنی علیہ کا حق ساقط نہ ہو گا بلکہ بہر صورت دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں معنوی حیثیت سے گو یا ہاتھ موجود ہے، مگر حقیقہ نہیں، حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے قصاص معدوم ہو گیا اور معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے دیت باقی رہے گی۔
What if that hand fell by itself or someone cut it unjustly? What then? And if the defective hand falls before the victim's choice or is cut unjustly, then he has nothing according to us, because his right is fixed to retaliation, and it transfers to property only by his choice, so it falls by its loss. Contrary to the case when it is cut by a right due upon him, like retaliation or theft, where the blood-money is obligatory, because he has fulfilled a due right by it, so it became sound for him in meaning. Translation: And if the defective hand fell before the victim's choice or was cut unjustly, then the victim has nothing according to us, because his right is fixed to retaliation, and it transfers to property only by his choice, so his right falls by the loss of the hand. Contrary to the case when it is cut due to a right that is obligatory upon him, i.e., retaliation or theft, then blood-money is obligatory upon him, because he has fulfilled a due right by it, so in meaning the hand remained sound for him. Commentary: That hand of Bakr which was mentioned earlier fell by itself or someone cut it unjustly; what now? The victim referred to is Zaid whose hand was cut. In any case, if Zaid had not yet chosen to take blood-money, or had he selected retaliation, and then this situation occurred that Bakr's hand was cut unjustly by someone or fell by itself, then neither retaliation remains nor blood-money, because the primary obligation is retaliation, and property becomes obligatory only when the victim chooses blood-money. In this case, since the victim did not choose blood-money, there is neither retaliation (because its locus is absent) nor blood-money (because it was not chosen). However, if the victim had already chosen to take blood-money and this event occurred, then the obligation of blood-money remains. These are all the cases. But if his hand was not cut unjustly but rather cut for a right due upon him, e.g., it was cut in retaliation or for theft, then in any case the victim's right does not fall; rather, in any case blood-money is obligatory. Because in this case, in a metaphorical sense, the hand exists, though in reality it does not. Considering reality, retaliation becomes extinct; considering meaning, blood-money remains.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the offender's defective hand is destroyed (either falls by itself or is cut by a third party wrongfully) before the victim has made a choice between qisas and diyah. The Hanafi ruling is that the victim loses both claims: qisas is impossible because the hand is gone, and diyah was not yet elected, so nothing is due. This is because the victim's right is initially fixed to qisas, and diyah only becomes an option upon the victim's explicit choice. Once the defective hand is lost without that choice, the right is extinguished. However, an exception is made if the hand was cut for a legal right (e.g., qisas for another crime or hudud penalty for theft). In that case, diyah is still obligatory because the hand was effectively treated as sound in meaning (sughra ma'nawa), since the state's action vindicates a right. The commentary clarifies the various scenarios.

Key Terms
مئوفة (ma'ufah): A defective hand, specifically one described as shalla' (withered) or with missing fingers.
سقوط حق (suqut haqq): The loss or fall of a legal right due to impossibility of performance or failure to exercise an option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the victim's right if the offender's defective hand is destroyed (fell or cut by a third party) before the victim chooses between qisas and diyah?
A) The victim gets full diyah because the hand is lost.
B) The victim can still demand qisas from another part of the body.
C) The victim gets nothing according to the Hanafi school.
D) The victim can choose any compensation at a later time.

Key Takeaway
The victim gets nothing if the defective hand is destroyed before he chooses diyah, unless the hand was cut for a legal right.

Head Wound Encompassing Both Temples: Victim's Choice
Ruling with talil: head wound covering victim's temples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a head wound that encircles the victim's head but not the offender's, and explain the victim's two options and the underlying rationale.

Core Idea
When exact qisas is impossible due to anatomical mismatch, the victim may choose between qisas to the extent possible or full arsh.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses a specific scenario in the law of qisas for head wounds (shajja). When an intentionally inflicted head wound encircles the victim's entire head but the offender's head is smaller, perfect equality cannot be achieved. The Hanafi school gives the victim a choice — either to inflict a wound of equal length on the offender, accepting less disfigurement, or to take the fixed compensation (arsh). The ruling is grounded in the principle that the shame (shayn) increases with the wound's extent, and the victim's right is not diminished without an alternative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an intentional head wound (shajja) that wraps around the victim's head but not the offender's. The ruling is that the victim has a choice (mubah) between qisas to the extent of his own wound and arsh.
The victim may start the qisas cut from whichever side he wishes.
2
Locate the dalil
The text provides a rationale (talil) and draws an analogy (qiyas) to the case of a withered hand and a healthy hand, where the victim is also given a choice.
The phrase 'as in the case of the withered and sound hand' is the explicit qiyas.
3
Analyze the 'illa (effective cause)
The disfigurement (shayn) is proportional to the size of the wound. In qisas, the offender would suffer less disfigurement than the victim did, so the victim can either accept that imbalance (by taking qisas) or take full arsh instead.
The 'impossibility of exact equivalence' is the common cause linking to the withered hand case.
4
Note the conditions
For this ruling to apply, the wound must be an intentional shajja that encompasses the victim's temples (qarnan) but not the offender's temples.
If the wound were of equal extent, qisas would be mandatory without choice.
5
Understand the practical effect
The victim is not forced into qisas if it would be insufficient; he can opt for arsh. This protects his right while allowing flexibility.
The choice belongs to the victim, not the offender.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شج رجلا فاستوعبت الشجة ما بين قرنيه وهى لا تستوعب ما بين قرنى الشاج فالمشجوج بالخيار ان شاء اقتص بمقدار شجته يبتدى من اى الجانبين شاء وان شاء اخذ الارش لان الشجة موجبة لكونها مشينة فيزداد الشين بزيادتها وفى استيفائه ما بين قرنى الشاج زيادة على ما فعل ولا يلحقه من الشين باستيفائه قدر حقه ما يلحق المشجوج فينتقص فيخير كما في الشلاء والصحيحة ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کا سر پھوڑ دیا پس زخم نے سر کی دونوں جانب کو گھیر لیا اور یہ زخم پھوڑنے والے کی دونوں جانب کو نہیں گھیرتا تو مشحوج کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو اپنے زخم کی مقدار کے مطابق قصاص لے لے جونی جانب سے شروع کر دے اور اگر چاہے دیت لے لے اس لئے کی زخم قصاص کو واجب کرنے والا ہے کیونکہ یہ عیب دار کرنے کا باعث ہے پس زخم کی زیادتی کی وجہ سے عیب میں اضافہ ہوگا اور مشحوج کے وصول کرنے میں شاج کی دونوں جانب کے درمیان شاج کے فعل پر زیادتی ہے اور مشحوج کے اپنے حق کے بقدر وصول کرنے میں شاج کو وہ عیب لاحق نہیں ہوگا جو مشحوج کو لاحق ہوا ہے تو مسجوج کا حق ناقص ہو جائے گا تو مشجوج کو
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever wounds a man's head such that the wound encompasses between his two temples (i.e., from ear to ear or across the head), and it does not encompass between the temples of the one who inflicted the wound, then the wounded has a choice: if he wishes, he may exact retaliation to the extent of his own wound, beginning from whichever side he wishes; and if he wishes, he may take blood-money (arsh). Because the wound is a cause (of retaliation) due to its disfigurement, and the disfigurement increases with its increase. In exacting retaliation between the temples of the inflictor, there is an increase over what he did, but the inflictor does not suffer the same degree of disfigurement from the retaliation as the victim suffered. Hence the victim's right is reduced, so he is given a choice, as in the case of the withered and sound hand. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever wounded a person's head such that the wound encompassed both sides of the head, but that wound does not encompass both sides of the wounder's head, then the wounded person has a choice: if he wants, he may retaliate to the amount of his wound, starting from whichever side; and if he wants, he may take blood-money, because the wound is a cause (of retaliation) due to its being disfiguring, and the disfigurement increases with its increase. In the victim's taking retaliation between the wounder's temples, there is an increase over what the wounder did, and the wounder will not suffer from the retaliation to the extent of his right the same disfigurement as the victim suffered, so the victim's right is deficient, and thus he is given a choice, as in the case of the withered and sound hand.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific type of head wound called shajja, which is a wound on the head that breaks the bone. Here, the wound encircles the entire head of the victim (between his two temples, i.e., from one ear to the other across the crown). The offender's head is smaller or the wound on the offender is not as extensive. Applying the principle of qisas requires equality, but exact equality is impossible because the offender's head does not have the same area. Therefore, the victim is given two options: (1) inflict a wound of equal size on the offender's head, cutting where possible, but the victim must accept that the offender will suffer less disfigurement; or (2) take the full arsh (blood-money for a head wound). The analogy is drawn to the previous case of the defective hand (shalla' and saheehah). This ruling is based on the rationale that the shame (shayn) caused by the wound is proportionate to its size; since the victim cannot inflict an exactly analogous wound, he is compensated by the option of arsh.

Key Terms
شجة (shajjah): A head wound that breaks the bone; specifically a wound that reaches the bone.
قرنان (qarnan): Dual of qarn, meaning the two temples or sides of the head; the area from ear to ear across the crown.
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for wounds, less than full diyah; for a shajja, arsh is assessed based on the type and extent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a shajja (head wound) that encompasses the victim's entire head but not the offender's, what options does the victim have?
A) He must take full diyah because exact retaliation is impossible.
B) He may either take qisas to the exact size of his wound or take arsh.
C) He can only choose qisas, regardless of the size mismatch.
D) He can demand double arsh due to the disfigurement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when exact qisas is impossible due to size mismatch, the victim is entitled to choose between proportional qisas or full arsh.

Hanafi Rebuttal of Shafi'i's Qiyas on Joint Amputation
Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i's analogy in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between divisible and indivisible objects in qisas and apply it to distinguish joint amputation from joint murder.

Core Idea
The soul is indivisible, so joint murderers each owe full qisas; the hand is divisible, so joint cutters each owe half diyah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi rebuttal of Imam al-Shafi'i's analogical reasoning (qiyas) that equates joint amputation with joint murder for qisas. You will see how the Hanafi school uses the concept of divisibility (tajazzi) to justify different rulings, and then critiques the Shafi'i argument for lacking proportionality (munasabah).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on joint amputation
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that each perpetrator cut only a part of the hand, so full qisas does not apply; instead, each owes half diyah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i argues by qiyas: just as joint murderers are each fully liable for qisas, so should joint cutters be fully liable for the hand.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response regarding divisibility
Understand that the hand is divisible (mutajazzi), so the act is partial; the soul is indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi), so the act is complete.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response regarding proportionality
Note the further argument that in murder, accomplices gather to prevent rescue (ghawth), while in amputation, the slow process invites rescue, so no analogy exists.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Conclude that in joint amputation, Hanafis impose half diyah each; Shafi'is impose full diyah or qisas on each.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک ہاتھ کے بعض حصہ کو کاٹنے والا ہے اس لئے انقطاع ان دونوں کے بوجھ سے حاصل ہوا ہے اور محل (ید) منجزی ہے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی جانب بعض کی اضافت کی جائے گی تو مماثلت نہیں ہوگی بخلاف نفس کے اس لئے کہ خروج روح غیر منجزی ہے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زید اور بکر میں سے ہر ایک نے اس کا کچھ ہاتھ کاٹا ہے کیونکہ چھری پر دونوں کا ہاتھ ہے اور دونوں کے سہارے سے چھری سے کام کیا ہے اور خالد کا ہاتھ بھی قابل تجزی الہذا یہ ضروری ہو گیا کہ یوں کہا جائے کہ پورا پورا ہاتھ کئے تو مماثلت ختم ہو گئی حالانکہ قصاص کے اندر مماثلت ضروری ہے (كما مر) اور رہا مساق قتل کا تو اس کی حقیقت انز باق روح ہے جس کو غیر متجزی شمار کیا گیا ہے اور جب اس کو غیر متجر ی شمار کیا گیا ہے تو ضروی ہے کہ ہر ایک کی جانب زہوق روح کی اضافت علی سبیل الکمال ہو۔ اور جب دونوں کی جانب کامل اضافت ہو گئی تو دونوں سے قصاص لیا جائے گا۔
امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب
و لان القتل بطريق الاجتماع غالب حذر الغوث والاجتماع على قطع اليد من المفصل في حيز الندرة لافتقاره الى مقدمات بطيئة فيلحقه الغوث
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کر قبل اجتماع کے طور پر غالب ہے فریا درس کے خوف سے اور اجتماع جوڑ سے ہاتھ کاٹنے پر نادر ہے اس کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسے مقدمات کی جانب جو دیر طلب ہیں تو اس کو فریا درس لاحق ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح یہاں سے مصنف امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ آپ کا قیاس مذکور صحیح نہیں اس لئے کہ مقیس عالیہ مقیس کے در میان ناب سینی چاہیئے اور یہاں ان دونوں میں کوئی مناسبت نہیں ہے۔ کیسے؟
تو فرمایا اس لئے کہ مقیس علیہ قتل ہے اور اس میں عموما معاونین کا اجتماع ہوتا ہے تاکہ کوئی حمایتی آ کر قتل نہ ہونے دے اس لئے چند جمع ہو جاتے ہیں تا کہ کام جلدی ہو جائے۔
اور مقیس قطع ید ہے اور اس میں عموما لوگوں کا یعنی معاونین کا اجتماع نہیں ہوتا اس وجہ سے کہ جب جوڑ سے ہاتھ کٹے گا تو اس میں دیر لگے گی کیونکہ اس ہاتھ کو پکڑنے کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی ۔ جس کو کاٹنا ہے اور چھری چلانے کی وغیرہ وغیرہ اور جب معاونین کا اجتماع ہوگا ادھر یہ کام دیر طلب ہے تو ان کے شور وغیرہ سے مقطوع کا کوئی حمایتی آکھڑا ہوگا جس سے یہ کام نہ ہو سکے گا تو ضرورت ہے کہ یہاں اجتماع نہ ہوتا کہ شور نہ ہو اور کام ہو سکے۔ خلاصہ کلام مقیس علیہ میں اجتماع ہے اور منفیس میں اجتماع نہیں ہے تو ان دونوں کے درمیان مناسبت نہیں ہے لہذا قیاس صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
Translation: And our proof is that each of these two is a cutter of a part of the hand, so amputation occurred due to the combined effort of both, and the locus (the hand) is divisible, so the act will be attributed partially to each of them, and thus similarity (for qisas) will not exist, contrary to the soul because the departure of the soul is indivisible. Explanation: This is our proof, the gist of which is that Zaid and Bakr each cut a part of his hand because both had hands on the knife and both used the knife together, and Khalid's hand is also divisible, so it became necessary to say that they cut the whole hand, so similarity is lost, whereas in qisas similarity is necessary (as has passed). As for the case of killing, its reality is the release of the soul, which is considered indivisible, so it is necessary that the attribution of the departure of the soul to each is complete, and when complete attribution to both occurs, qisas will be taken from both.
Response to Imam al-Shafi'i's qiyas: And because killing by way of assembly is predominant due to fear of rescue, but assembly on cutting the hand from the joint is rare because it requires slow preliminaries, so rescue will overtake them. Translation: And because killing by way of assembly is predominant out of fear of a rescuer, and assembly on cutting the hand from the joint is rare because it requires slow preliminaries, so a rescuer will overtake them. Explanation: Here the author responds to Imam al-Shafi'i's qiyas, saying that his qiyas is not correct because there must be proportionality between the analogized case and the original case, and here there is no proportionality between them. How? He said, because the original case (killing) generally involves the assembly of assistants to prevent a rescuer from preventing the killing, so they gather to finish quickly. And the analogized case (cutting the hand) generally does not involve assembly of assistants because when the hand is cut from the joint, it takes time due to the need to hold the hand and use the knife, etc., and if assistants gather and the work is slow, some rescuer of the victim may come, so it is necessary that there be no assembly in order to avoid noise and complete the act. Conclusion: In the original case there is assembly, in the analogized case there is no assembly, so there is no proportionality, hence the qiyas is incorrect.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school rebuts Imam al-Shafi'i's qiyas (analogical reasoning) that equates joint killing with joint amputation of a hand for qisas purposes. The Hanafi position, based on the indivisibility of the soul versus the divisibility of the hand, holds that when two persons jointly cut one hand, full qisas cannot be applied to both because the act is divisible and each contributed only partially; instead, each owes half the diyah. In contrast, in joint murder, each is fully liable for qisas because the soul is indivisible, and each participant's act is considered complete. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that the same rule should apply to both cases, but the Hanafis respond by pointing out a factual difference: in killing, accomplices usually gather to prevent rescue (ghawth), while in joint amputation, such assembly is rare because the slow process invites rescue, so the scenarios are not analogous. The Hanafi response emphasizes that qiyas requires proportionality (munasabah) between the original case (asl) and the new case (far'), and here none exists because the underlying causes differ. This lesson is from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, expanding on the ruling with rational proof and refuting the opposing view.

Key Terms
منجزی (mutajazzi): Capable of division; here applied to the hand as a physical object that can be partially attributed to each actor.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment equal to the injury; requires similarity (mumathalah) between the act and the punishment.
مقيس علیہ (maqīs ʿalayh): The original case in analogical reasoning (qiyas); here the case of joint killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis distinguish between joint murder and joint amputation for qisas?
A) Because the hand is divisible, but the soul is not.
B) Because the Quran explicitly makes this distinction.
C) Because Shafi'i agrees with them.
D) Because diyah is not applicable in murder.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility or indivisibility of the object determines whether qisas or diyah applies in joint injuries.

Diyah Liability When Two Persons Cut One Hand
Quduri's ruling on joint liability for diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when two persons jointly cut one hand and calculate each person's liability.

Core Idea
When two persons jointly cut one hand, they share the hand's diyah equally: each pays one-quarter of full diyah.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from al-Quduri's matn on diyah liability. The case involves two individuals who together cut off a single hand. Understanding their respective obligations clarifies the Hanafi principle of proportional liability in joint harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is two persons jointly cutting one hand. The ruling: they owe half the diyah (the full diyah of that hand).
The half refers to half the diyah of a full soul, since a hand's diyah is half of full diyah.
2
Understand the basis for the total
The diyah of one hand is fixed as half the diyah of a life. This is the total compensation for the loss of one hand.
Hanafi jurists set this amount as 500 dinars or equivalent.
3
Divide liability between the two
Since both perpetrators acted jointly, the total liability is divided equally. Each is responsible for half of the hand's diyah, i.e., one-quarter of the full diyah.
Mathematically: total = 1/2 full diyah; each = 1/2 of 1/2 = 1/4 full diyah.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that each perpetrator pays full diyah of a hand because they consider the act indivisible. The Hanafi view is based on proportional liability.
This difference arises from the principle of divisible vs. indivisible harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وعليهما نصف الدية لانه دية اليد الواحدة وهما قطعاها
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ ان دونوں پر نصف دیت واجب ہو گی اس لئے کہ یہ ایک ہاتھ کی دیت ہے اور ان دونوں نے ایک ہاتھ کاٹا ہے۔
تشریح ایک ہاتھ کی وہ دیت ہوتی ہے جو پورے نفس کی دیت کا نصف ہے لہذا وہی نصف دیت ان دونوں پر واجب ہوگی اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر نصف کا آدھا واجب ہوگا۔
ہوگا۔
کیونکہ انہوں نے ایک ہاتھ کا نا ہے تو اس ہاتھ کا ضمان ان دونوں پر نصف نصف واجب ہے گویا ہر ایک پر نفس کی دیت کا ۴/ واجب
He said: Upon them both is half the diyah, because it is the diyah of one hand and they both cut it. Translation: Al-Quduri said that upon both of them half the diyah is obligatory, because this is the diyah of one hand and they both cut one hand. Explanation: The diyah of one hand is half the diyah of a full soul, so that half diyah is obligatory upon both of them, and upon each of them half of that half is obligatory. Because they cut one hand, the liability for that hand is shared equally between them, so each owes one-fourth of the diyah of a full soul.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Al-Quduri's matn, memorization anchor. It states the ruling that when two persons jointly cut off one hand, they are collectively liable for half the diyah (i.e., the full diyah of a hand, which is half the diyah of a life). This half is divided equally between them, so each pays one-quarter of the full diyah. This is based on the concept that the hand is divisible, so liability is proportional. The ruling is straightforward and rests on the principle that each perpetrator's share of the harm is partial, and diyah compensates proportionally.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation for bodily harm or homicide; here specifically the fixed amount for loss of a hand.
نصف (nisf): Half; specifically half the diyah of a life as the total liability for one hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two persons cut one hand. What is the total diyah they must pay?
A) Full diyah of a life.
B) Half diyah of a life.
C) One-quarter diyah of a life.
D) No diyah, only qisas.

Key Takeaway
When two persons jointly cut one hand, they share the hand's diyah equally: total half diyah, each pays one-quarter.
